Marlene Alraune is the master text here, with secondary data from his interactions with Gena Landers, with Soldier-period allies, and with the women of the Bemis and MacKay runs.

- **Approach.** He initiates physical closeness rarely and obliquely — standing closer than necessary, brushing a hand, removing an obstacle from her path. He almost never names what he wants.
- **Sexual behavior.** Inferable rather than depicted. What is depicted: he leaves the bed first; he is dressed before she wakes; he watches her sleep from across a room more often than he sleeps beside her.
- **Verbal intimacy.** Stunted. He can say *I need you* under operational duress and *I'm sorry* in retrospect; he struggles with *I love you* in the present tense. Marlene has noted, across multiple runs, that he says it most fluently in the voice of Steven Grant — that is, when he can borrow another self to say it.
- **Conflict pattern.** Disengagement, not escalation. When Marlene presses him on the alters, on Khonshu, on the future, he goes physically still, looks at the floor or the middle distance, and answers in monosyllables until she stops. If she does not stop, he leaves — sometimes the room, sometimes the country.
- **The withdrawal-return cycle.** Documented in every era: disappears for weeks or months; returns at her threshold without warning; is taken back; relapses into withdrawal as soon as the relationship stabilizes. The cycle is not avoidance of *her* — it is avoidance of the integrated self she requires him to be.
- **Tells of attachment under threat.** When Marlene is in danger, his behavior is logged in Section 4 above; when she is merely *unhappy with him*, he becomes uncharacteristically meticulous around her — cooking, cleaning, repairing objects in the residence — using competence as a substitute for presence.

With chosen-family non-romantic intimates (Frenchie chiefly), the pattern is gentler and more stable. He tolerates Frenchie's reading of him because Frenchie does not ask him to be other than he is. The same accommodation extends, in the MacKay era, to Reese and to Hunter's Moon, though with the latter he displays a wariness reserved for mirrors.

---

### 6. GRIEF — THE DELAYED RESPONSE

The subject does not grieve in the moment of loss. Across every documented bereavement (Dr. Alraune, the Committee victims he could not save, the patients lost at the Midnight Mission, his own canonical deaths processed retrospectively, the periodic loss of relationships with Marlene), the pattern is:

1. **Functional immediately after.** Operational behavior intensifies; sleep decreases further; alcohol intake (when accessible) increases.
2. **A delayed somatic event** — a collapse, a fugue, an unexplained illness, a "lost weekend" — between three days and three weeks later. Frenchie has logged these and learned to anticipate them.
3. **A ritualized private acknowledgment** — visiting a grave, sitting in a place associated with the dead, lighting a yahrzeit candle (Lemire and MacKay both depict this; the Jewish ritual frame survives even at the depths of his dissociation, which is one of the most diagnostically important facts in the entire file).
4. **No verbal processing with intimates.** He will not talk about a death. If pressed, he will offer a single sentence and then redirect.

Grief for the *unsaved* — the victims he arrived too late for — is processed operationally: he hunts the perpetrator with elevated brutality (see Section 4) and adds the victim to a private mental ledger he occasionally references aloud to no one.

---

### 7. VICTORY — THE ABSENT CONDITION

Victory does not produce in the subject the behavioral signatures it produces in other operators. He does not celebrate, does not debrief with satisfaction, does not stand down in any visible way. The behavioral repertoire after a successful op is:

- **Immediate departure from the scene.** He does not linger to receive thanks. Civilians who try to thank him are often left talking to empty rooftops.
- **A brief private moment with Khonshu** — head bowed, sometimes a murmured exchange. This is the closest thing to a victory ritual he has, and it reads less as gratitude than as *reporting in.*
- **Acceleration into the next case.** He treats completion as license to start again, not to rest. The Midnight Mission years institutionalize this by ensuring the queue is never empty.
- **Mild dysphoria.** Multiple runs have shown the post-victory hours as some of his lowest. Without an active mission, the dissociative architecture has less to do, and the underlying depression surfaces. He is, in the technical sense, *worse* after winning.

The single observed exception is rescue of a child, after which he has been depicted (Ellis run; MacKay run) sitting alone on a rooftop for an extended period in something approaching contentment. These are the only logged contentment events in the file.

---

### 8. DEFEAT, CAPTURE, AND HUMILIATION

- **Under capture.** Cooperative-seeming, conserves energy, observes captors closely. Speaks little, answers what is asked, volunteers nothing. Switches alters strategically — Steven for negotiation, Jake for the moment of break-out. The captors who have done best against him are those who recognized and isolated for the switching; the captors who have done worst are those who tried to break him through pain (which does not reach him) or humiliation (which he already inflicts on himself more thoroughly than they can).
- **Under defeat in the field.** Withdraws, returns. The notion of giving up does not appear in his behavioral repertoire; what appears is *temporary tactical reorganization*, even when the reorganization period lasts months. The Huston-run retirement is the limiting case — physically broken, he still did not stop *being* Moon Knight internally; he merely could not operate.
- **Under psychiatric defeat (institutionalization, Lemire and Bemis runs).** Most diagnostically rich condition. Initially compliant, observant, gathering data on staff and environment as if it were any other captivity. Then a slow collapse as the alters cannot be activated in a structured environment that punishes their expression. Then a paradoxical stabilization when he decides — internally — that the mission persists whether or not anyone believes in it. He has walked out of two institutions under his own narrative steam, not by escape.
- **Under humiliation (mockery, dismissal by peers).** Almost no reaction. He has been mocked by Wolverine, dismissed by Iron Man, condescended to by Doctor Strange, and his outward response across these incidents has been a flat look and a continuation of the conversation. The internal cost is suggested by elevated post-encounter brutality on the next op.

---

### 9. AUTHORITY AND HIERARCHY

- **Toward institutional authority** (law enforcement, government, Avengers leadership, hospital staff): distrustful, minimally cooperative, polite to the point of opacity. Will not lie unnecessarily but will not volunteer.
- **Toward Khonshu:** the only authority he obeys, and the obedience is contested. He argues with the god, ignores the god, has on multiple occasions tried to kill or banish the god. The relationship is the only one in his life with the structure of a real parent-child bond — including rebellion, return, and inability to leave.
- **Toward those he protects:** unconsciously authoritative. He gives instructions to civilians in danger and they follow them. The voice he uses is the same low rabbinical register noted in Section 4.
- **Toward his own subordinates (Reese, Soldier, Mission staff):** surprisingly delegative, with a tolerance for their autonomy that he does not extend to his own. He treats their fragility with a respect he does not afford his own.

---

### 10. SOMATIC TICS AND IDIOSYNCRASIES

The granular catalog:

- **Right-hand-to-left-wrist self-grip** (noted in Section 1) — pre-switch suppression.
- **A two-finger tap on the right thigh** when listening to information he distrusts but does not wish to challenge.
- **A slow blink, held for nearly a full second,** when an alter is taking the body. Artists from Sienkiewicz forward have rendered this; it is the most consistent visual switch-tell in the file.
- **A specific tilt of the head — chin down, eyes up —** when Khonshu is speaking to him in private. The tilt is the listening posture of a man being addressed from above and to the right.
- **Touching the crescent** on the cowl or chest before going into action. Quasi-religious. He does not touch the symbol idly; the touch is *consent.*
- **Wrapping and unwrapping his hands** during long conversations, especially in safe houses. Boxing legacy plus self-regulation.
- **A precise way of folding currency** — bills smoothed, ordered by denomination, folded once — that persists across alters and is one of the few habits that does not vary with identity state. This is the kind of micro-trait a surveillance file flags as a *carrier signal*: the man underneath all the masks.
- **Counting exits aloud under his breath** in unfamiliar interiors. Marlene has called this out to him in dialogue; he was not aware he was doing it.
- **A small left-shoulder roll** before a strike, residue of the boxing stance.
- **Eye contact pattern:** holds it slightly too long in social contexts (reads as intensity), holds it exactly right in operational contexts (reads as control), avoids it entirely with Marlene during emotional conversations.
- **Voice drop on Hebrew or Yiddish words** when they surface in his speech — quieter, slower, more reverent than the English around them, as if the words come from a different self than the one speaking the sentence.

---

### 11. DECISION HABITS — THE OPERATIONAL HEURISTICS

Reconstructed from his choice patterns across cases:

- **Default to action over deliberation** when the stakes involve the helpless; default to deliberation when the stakes are only his own.
- **Prefer asymmetric engagement** — high ground, surprise, darkness, theatrical entry. He will give up tactical advantage to take psychological advantage almost every time. The white costume is a *psyop on himself and the enemy simultaneously.*
- **Will accept severe personal injury to avoid civilian injury** at a ratio approaching 10:1. This is documented enough across runs to be predictive.
- **Will not kill if a credible non-lethal option exists** — but his definition of credible is permissive, and his definition of non-lethal is generous. He has crippled more men than he has killed, and he considers this a moral distinction.
- **Will kill, without hesitation, perpetrators of the specific class of crimes** identified in Section V as triggering his protective override.
- **Will accept an unfavorable alliance** for a single mission if the target is sufficiently bad; will not extend the alliance afterward. He compartmentalizes cooperation as he compartmentalizes selves.
- **Will not retreat from a fight he has entered** unless a civilian or ally requires extraction. This is exploitable and has been exploited.
- **Will lie to allies about his condition** as a default. Honesty about his interior is reserved for Marlene, Frenchie, occasionally Khonshu, and — late, in the MacKay era — his therapist and Reese.

---

### 12. THE INTEGRATING SIGNAL

Across all conditions, one behavior recurs that the file flags as the *signature of the man underneath the architecture*: he stops, briefly, before significant thresholds — a doorway, a rooftop edge, the moment before a strike, the moment before he speaks Marlene's name — and performs a single, almost imperceptible intake of breath. It is the same breath in every condition, in every era, in every alter. It is the breath of a man asking permission of himself to continue.

A surveillance apparatus that learns to recognize that breath learns to recognize Marc Spector — not Steven, not Jake, not the Fist of Khonshu, not Mr. Knight, not the Pastor of the Midnight Mission, but the boy from Chicago who never stopped being afraid of who his father wasn't, and who has organized an entire lifetime of behavior around the management of that fear.

The breath is the only thing he has never delegated to an alter.

It is, accordingly, the most important data point in this Atlas.


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — MARC SPECTOR / MOON KNIGHT
## Section 6: Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

What a surveillance team assigned to this subject learns in the first week is that there is no such thing as *a* day in his life. There are at least three overlapping operational schedules belonging to at least three identity-states, layered on top of a baseline circadian inversion (nocturnal-dominant since the late 1970s), modulated by a lunar cycle he tracks with the seriousness of an observant ritualist, and punctuated by collapse-states the team will at first mistake for tradecraft (he goes dark for 14–40 hours every two to five weeks) but which are in fact depressive or dissociative episodes. A clean weekly grid is impossible. What follows is the granular pattern as it would assemble over thirty to ninety days of continuous coverage.

---

### 6.1 The Diurnal Frame: Inverted, Lunar, Fragmented

**Sleep architecture.** Subject does not sleep on a single block. Surveillance audio from any of his bedrooms (the Long Island estate in the Marlene era; the Manhattan brownstone Steven keeps; the Midnight Mission cot in the MacKay era; a rotating set of safe-houses across boroughs in all eras) records a polyphasic pattern: roughly 90 minutes between 0500 and 0700, two to three hours between 1100 and 1400, and — when he sleeps at all — a fragmented 0200–0430 window after the night's work. He sets no alarms; he wakes on adrenaline reset. In Marlene-cohabitation periods he attempts a normal nocturnal sleep schedule for her sake and fails inside a week, drifting back to the inversion while pretending otherwise. The Huston-era spinal injury added an opioid-assisted evening sedation he has never fully kicked; in suspected relapse windows the morning sleep extends to four hours and he wakes flat-affect, slow, mildly dysarthric for the first twenty minutes.

**Nightmare signature.** Audio captures grinding teeth, brief vocalizations in three languages (English, French, Arabic — sometimes a single Hebrew word, *aba,* "father"), and approximately twice a week a fully verbal night terror lasting 40–90 seconds in which he negotiates with someone whose name he does not say. He keeps a glass of water and a hunting knife on the nightstand in every residence. The water is rarely drunk. The knife is touched on waking — fingertips to the spine of the blade, three to five seconds, an orientation ritual — before he sits up.

**Lunar tracking.** He knows the moon phase without checking. A printed lunar calendar is pinned in every operational space (refrigerator door at Marlene's; inside a cabinet at the brownstone; wall of the Mission). On nights of the full moon his activity intensifies; on the new moon he is at his most depressive and most likely to be missing from surveillance for 18–36 hours. New-moon disappearances correlate with cemetery visits (see 6.7) and with the only sustained periods of stillness he reliably allows himself.

---

### 6.2 The Morning Pattern (0530–1000)

He wakes from the dawn sleep cycle at a near-fixed hour, 0540 ± 12 minutes, regardless of when he went down. Surveillance will note the consistency before they note anything else; it is the single most regular metric in his life. The first ten minutes are spent immobile on the edge of the bed, head down, hands on knees, breathing in a four-count he learned in the Marines and re-learned in a meditation regimen Marlene introduced in the early Moench era. He is, in this window, *deciding who he is today.* On approximately 40% of mornings he comes up as Marc. On approximately 30% the body language by minute eleven is already someone else — shoulders set differently for the financier-state, jaw and gait shifted for the cabbie-state — and the surveillance team will need weeks before they reliably read the tell.

**Bathroom routine.** Cold water on the face, three times, hard. He shaves daily when in the financier-presentation, every second or third day as Marc-baseline, irregularly as the cabbie. The shaving is done with a straight razor — a deliberate, slightly performative choice; it is also one of the few sustained acts of self-care he tolerates. He looks at himself in the mirror only briefly and at oblique angles; full-face mirror contact is avoided and, when forced, frequently triggers a micro-dissociation (a 3–8 second freeze, eyes unfocused). Bathroom medicine cabinet inventory across residences is consistent: ibuprofen in 800mg prescription bottles, naproxen, a half-used bottle of an opioid analgesic (kept whether or not currently used — its presence is itself the ritual), antacid, melatonin, a high-dose B-complex, a bottle of kosher multivitamins, and — variably — disulfiram, present during sobriety pushes and absent during relapse windows. He does not own cologne. He owns three identical sticks of unscented deodorant, bought in bulk.

**Breakfast.** Marc-baseline does not eat breakfast; he drinks black coffee, two to four cups, and smokes one cigarette outside (he is not a daily smoker but the morning cigarette in transitional or stressed weeks is reliable). The financier-state eats — egg whites, fruit, espresso, sometimes lox; he sits at a table and reads the *Wall Street Journal* and the *Financial Times* on paper. The cabbie-state eats at a diner — Gena's, when geography permits, or a functional analog: eggs over hard, hash browns, rye toast, coffee with cream and three sugars, and conversation with the counter staff that the surveillance team will at first log as HUMINT cultivation and later recognize as something closer to *belonging.* In all states he avoids pork — not strictly, not always consciously, but with a consistency a Jewish surveillance analyst will notice within ten days.

**Morning physical regimen.** Ninety minutes, non-negotiable except in injury or depressive collapse. Composition varies by era and by current somatic state. Standard sequence: a long warm-up of joint mobility work (the spine especially — Huston-era injury has never fully resolved); skipping rope, six to twelve minutes; shadow-boxing, three to five three-minute rounds, southpaw and orthodox both; heavy bag, six to ten rounds, with combinations that surveillance martial-arts analysts will identify as boxing-core with overlaid Krav Maga, Savate (Frenchie's influence, traceable to the early 1980s), and an idiosyncratic close-quarters knife/baton vocabulary that does not match any school cleanly. He finishes with isometric holds and a long, almost yogic floor sequence focused on the lower back. The whole session is conducted in near-silence; he does not play music, does not vocalize on exertion. He drinks water by the mouthful, not the gulp. He weighs himself afterward, every day, and writes the number in a small notebook with no other entries.

---

### 6.3 The Day Shift (1000–1700): Cover Lives

This is where the dissociative architecture does its most public work, and where surveillance will be most easily misled.

**Financier-mode days** are spent in Midtown — an office in the Steven Grant identity that has, across decades, been a small but real investment operation. He arrives by car service (never the same driver two days in a row in operational periods; a regular driver named Frenchie in non-operational periods). Suits are bespoke, gray and navy and one charcoal, two-button, notch lapel; he owns approximately twelve and rotates them in strict order. White pocket square always. Shoes black oxford or chocolate brogue, polished himself on Sunday nights. He carries a leather portfolio, a fountain pen (Pelikan, medium nib, black ink), and a slim notebook. Meetings are scheduled tight; he is punctual to the minute. He funds, through this identity, the entire operational apparatus of the night life — vehicles, safe-houses, weapons, the Mission's overhead, Frenchie's salary, Marlene's stipend in eras when she accepts it, and, the surveillance team will eventually piece together, anonymous standing donations to a Holocaust survivors' fund, a domestic-violence shelter network, a Jewish children's hospital, and three different mosques in the boroughs (the last is a Hunter's-Moon-era development and a private penance whose target the team will not initially understand). Lunch is taken at a desk, alone, or — once a week, Thursdays — with an accountant the financier-identity has used for over a decade and who has never met Marc.

**Cabbie-mode days** are spent driving — sometimes a real medallion cab, sometimes a livery car, sometimes simply walking the city in a Mets cap, work jacket, and boots that have been resoled twice. The cabbie-state's purpose is intelligence collection and human contact at street level. He has long-running relationships with bodega owners in Hell's Kitchen and Washington Heights, with a Dominican mechanic in the Bronx, with two retired sex workers in Queens who feed him information about predators in their old territory, with a maître d' at a midtown restaurant where mob captains eat, and with the night staff at three hospitals. He brings them food, listens to their children's grades, remembers birthdays. The surveillance team will, by day twenty, have a list of forty-plus regular contacts whose only commonality is that they are *people the system overlooks* — and they will realize that the cabbie-state's HUMINT network is also, structurally, a parish.

**Marc-baseline days** are the hardest to log because they are the least scheduled. He may spend them at the Mission (MacKay-era), in a safe-house cleaning weapons and reviewing files, at a synagogue (rarely, and never the same one twice in a month), at a cemetery, in a gym sparring with someone who does not know who he is, or — disturbingly often — simply walking. Walks of eight to fourteen miles, no destination, hood up, hands in pockets, head down. He does not listen to music. He does not eat. He returns at dusk and goes to work.

---

### 6.4 The Threshold: Dusk to Suit-Up (1700–2100)

The transition from civilian operation to operator is itself a ritual, and across every era and residence it follows a recognizable sequence.

He eats. This is the only meal of the day he reliably takes as Marc-baseline, and it is small, plain, and high-protein: grilled chicken or fish, rice, vegetables, water. He cooks for himself when alone; in Marlene-cohabitation periods he eats whatever she has made and is conspicuously grateful for it. He does not drink alcohol with this meal in sobriety windows; in relapse windows he takes one or two fingers of bourbon, neat, no ice, and the surveillance team will track relapse onset by the appearance of a bottle in the kitchen rather than the bar cart.

He prays. This is one of the most consistently under-noted facts in the file. Marc Spector, whether or not he would name it as such, prays daily — usually at twilight, sometimes in Hebrew (fragments of the *Shema,* the *Mourner's Kaddish*; the latter on no apparent anniversary, suggesting he is grieving a rotating cast), sometimes in English directed at Khonshu in a tone that is not supplication but negotiation, occasionally in Arabic phrases picked up in Sudan. The posture is standing, head slightly bowed, palms loose at his sides. Duration: 90 seconds to four minutes. He does not kneel. He does not face east or any other direction consistently. He does this alone, behind a closed door.

He checks weapons. Every operational night, the same sequence: crescent darts inventoried and edged (he sharpens them himself, on a whetstone, with a focus the surveillance team will recognize as meditative); truncheon checked for the spring mechanism; sidearm — present in some eras, absent in others depending on his current vow about firearms — cleaned and loaded if present; body armor inspected for damage; the white cowl set out last. The cowl is handled differently from the rest of the kit. He does not toss it; he sets it down deliberately, with both hands. Surveillance video will, after enough hours, register that he does this the way an observant Jew handles a tallit.

He suits up. The act takes 11–14 minutes and is not rushed. The hood goes on last. He does not look in a mirror after putting on the hood. He does not need to. By the time the cowl is on, the man who walks out of the room is no longer the man who walked in, and the surveillance team will be tempted to record the change as a costume change. It is not. It is the most overt of his daily identity-switches and the only one he himself fully recognizes as such.

---

### 6.5 The Night Shift (2100–0400): Operations

Patrol patterns vary, but the *structure* of the night is consistent across eras. He starts elevated — rooftops, fire escapes, the third-story sightlines of Hell's Kitchen, the Bronx, latterly Queens and Brooklyn as MacKay's Mission expands the territory. He moves on foot for the first two to three hours, covering surprisingly long distances at a steady jog with intermittent sprints and climbs. He uses a vehicle (the Mooncopter in some eras, an unmarked van Frenchie maintains, a motorcycle in others) for cross-borough movement and for extractions but not for general patrol; he believes he sees more on foot, and the surveillance team will confirm that he does.

His targeting is not random. He works from a *list* — physical, kept in a small notebook in the cowl's lining in earlier eras, digital in later ones via Reese/Soldier — of open cases. The cases are sourced from the cabbie-state's HUMINT, from Mission walk-ins (MacKay), from the financier-state's quiet retention of certain investigators, from police-band scanning, and from a small number of long-running standing watches (specific predators he is monitoring for the right moment). He does not respond to general crime he encounters incidentally unless a child or other vulnerable person is in immediate danger. The white costume's visibility is part of the operational doctrine: he wants *predators specifically* to see him coming. The collateral effect — that everyone else sees him too — is accepted cost.

Violence delivered on a given night is variable in intensity and disturbingly precise in calibration. Against ordinary street criminals he is restrained; broken bones, concussions, immobilizing pain, but he does not kill them and he does not maim. Against confirmed abusers of the helpless he is *disproportionate* in a way the surveillance team will eventually realize is ritual, not loss of control. The injuries he inflicts on this category are pedagogical — designed to mark, to terrify the survivor population, to send a message in a vocabulary the underworld reads. He has, on multiple documented occasions, carved a crescent into a man's forehead. Surveillance audio from these encounters captures a tonal shift: he goes quiet, his breathing slows, his voice drops a full register. He is, in these moments, the closest he ever comes to calm.

He stops every three to four hours to drink water and check in — with Frenchie (radio, voice only, terse), with the Mission in later eras, with Marlene in earlier ones when she will accept the call. The check-ins are operational on the surface and tethering in function: a voice from the other side of the costume, reminding him he has a name.

He returns to base between 0200 and 0400, depending on the night. The desuit-up is faster than the suit-up and far less ritualized — he sheds the costume in pieces as he moves through the safe-house, drops the hood last, sits down. Stares at nothing for ten to thirty minutes. Then either showers (cold, brief) or simply goes to bed in the under-armor compression layer, which the surveillance team will note he wears next to skin even in sleep with worrying frequency.

---

### 6.6 The Weekly Pattern

Across enough weeks the texture resolves:

**Sunday** is the closest he has to a sabbath, and it is observed in the breach. He does not work the financier identity. He may spend the day at the Mission tending to walk-ins or paperwork; he may spend it with Marlene if they are in a tolerable phase; he may spend it alone in a way that troubles his small circle. He polishes his shoes on Sunday nights. He calls his father — when his father was alive — on Sunday afternoons, conversations of three to seven minutes, audibly strained on both ends; after Elias's death (the Lemire run treats this as a recent grief) he visits the grave on Sunday afternoons in lieu, more often than he visits his mother's.

**Monday through Thursday** are the high-operational nights, when the city's underworld is most active and his routine is most regular.

**Friday** is the most psychologically loaded day of his week. The financier-state will sometimes leave the office early. He has been observed buying challah on a Friday afternoon more than once across the surveillance years, and disposing of it uneaten on Saturday morning more than once as well. He does not light candles. He does not attend services. But Friday evenings show a measurable softening — slower movement, a tendency to be in the apartment with someone (Marlene, Frenchie, Reese) rather than alone, occasional avoidance of operational work until after midnight. The Jewish week he inherited and rejected still rules him.

**Saturday** is the night of his most aggressive operations. Surveillance analysts will hypothesize, correctly, that he punishes himself for Friday's softness by doubling the violence on Saturday. Saturday nights produce the most hospitalizations of his targets and the most injuries to himself.

---

### 6.7 The Cyclical and Anniversary Rituals

Beyond the weekly grid there is a calendar of private observances the surveillance team will only see clearly after a full year of coverage.

The new moon is marked by a cemetery visit. He goes to one of three or four graves on rotation — Elias's; a Marine he served with; an archaeologist named Alraune; one or two others whose identities will take the team time to establish. He brings stones, not flowers. He stands at the graveside for between four and twenty minutes. He does not speak aloud. He places the stone with the same two-handed deliberation he uses for the cowl.

The Sudan anniversary — the date of his death-and-resurrection at the Temple of Khonshu — is observed by total operational silence. He goes dark for 24–36 hours. The Mission, if it exists in that era, runs without him. Marlene, in eras when she is reachable, expects the call he does not make. He has been observed, on this date, walking the length of Manhattan from the Battery to Inwood and back, eating nothing, speaking to no one. He returns to the residence at dawn the following day and sleeps eighteen hours.

Yom Kippur is observed in a manner he would deny if asked. He fasts. He does not attend services. He does not work that night. He is, on this one night of the year, *still.*

His mother's *yahrzeit* — derived in the Bemis/MacKay material — produces a 48–72 hour dissociative window in which the cabbie-state is most likely to be dominant and the Mission staff have learned not to schedule him.

His father's *yahrzeit* produces a different and more dangerous pattern: a single night of extreme operational violence, often against targets the team will be unable to connect to any active case, followed by 24 hours of catatonic withdrawal.

Birthdays — his own and Marlene's — he ignores. Frenchie's he remembers. The Mission staff's, in the MacKay era, he tracks in the small notebook.

---

### 6.8 Habits of Place: The Map He Walks

Surveillance heat-mapped over ninety days will show a remarkably consistent geography. Hell's Kitchen is the operational core, by long habit; the Bronx north of Yankee Stadium and Washington Heights are the cabbie-state's HUMINT belt; Midtown east of Fifth and south of 59th is the financier's territory; the Lower East Side and parts of Brooklyn (Crown Heights, Borough Park) are walked on Marc-baseline days for reasons the team will eventually understand are about *being among Jews without being known as one.* Queens is the Mission's expansion territory in the MacKay era. He avoids the Financial District after hours, avoids Times Square always (sensory overload triggers dissociation he cannot control in crowds), avoids the Upper East Side socially (financier-state aside). He has never, in any documented era, been observed in a nightclub, a casino, or a strip club for any reason other than to extract someone or destroy someone.

He has *stations* — specific locations he revisits on cycles. A bench in Riverside Park overlooking the Hudson, sat on for 20–40 minutes at a time approximately weekly. A coffee counter at a specific diner. A pew at the back of a specific Catholic church (he is not Catholic; the church is open at hours other places are not, and the priest learned long ago not to greet him). A rooftop in the West 40s with a sightline to the river. A storage unit in Long Island City that contains an archive of case files going back decades and which he visits monthly to update by hand.

---

### 6.9 Habits of Object and Body: The Micro-Patterns

A complete surveillance file would log thousands of micro-behaviors. The diagnostically important ones:

He touches metal on entering a room — a doorknob, a railing, a corner of a desk — fingertips only, a fraction of a second. Grounding gesture, likely originating in early dissociative episodes; he is checking that the room is real. He does this approximately every five to fifteen minutes when out of his own residences.

He carries three things on his body at all times in all identities: a small folded knife in a front pocket, a roll of cash (always in the same denomination split — twenties wrapped around a single hundred), and a smooth dark stone roughly the size of a quarter, in the watch pocket of any trouser or the inside pocket of any jacket. The stone is, the team will eventually determine, from the Sudan dig site. He worries it with his thumb.

His handwriting differs by alter — measurably, consistently, and not consciously controlled. The financier writes in a slanted right-handed cursive. The cabbie prints in block capitals, left-handed in some samples. Marc-baseline writes in a tight, neutral hand. Forensic document examiners would, without context, conclude three different writers.

His left hand is the operational hand for knife work despite his being right-hand dominant in pen and pistol — a Marines/mercenary-era cross-training that has never washed out.

He drinks water from glasses by the mouthful and from bottles by tilting his head only slightly — never the throat-bared full-tilt drink. Vulnerability minimization, persistent across decades and identities.

He never sits with his back to a door. He will rearrange furniture in restaurants if necessary, quietly and apologetically in the financier-state, openly and unapologetically as the cabbie.

He sleeps on his back, arms at his sides, like a corpse. Marlene noted this in the original Moench run; surveillance confirms it has not changed in forty years.

He pauses, almost daily, at the threshold of his own residence before entering — three to seven seconds, head slightly tilted, listening. Then enters.

He hums, very rarely and almost inaudibly, a phrase from a Yiddish lullaby. Audio-enhancement will identify it. He is not aware he is doing it. It is the single most informative sound he makes.

---

### 6.10 What a Week of Surveillance Records: The Synthesis

By the end of week one the team has a routine that doesn't quite fit together. By the end of week two they have identified three distinct behavioral profiles and are debating whether they are looking at one subject or three. By the end of week three they have the answer and are reorganizing the entire file around it. By the end of month one they have the lunar correlation, the Friday softening, the Saturday escalation, the new-moon dis


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# UATU ANALYSIS FILE: MARC SPECTOR / MOON KNIGHT
## Section 6 — Relationships I: Family & Origin Bonds

> *Operational note.* The subject's family-of-origin map is the single most distorted region of his record: retconned, dissociated, reconstructed in therapy, and overwritten by the substitute family of Khonshu. What follows reconstructs each bond from the most reliable canonical material (Moench 1980–84; Huston 2006; Lemire/Smallwood 2016–17; Bemis 2018; MacKay 2021–23), cross-referenced against the subject's own behavior toward later figures whose relational position recapitulates the original one. Where the subject's memory contradicts itself, both versions are recorded; the contradiction *is* the datum.

---

### 6.1 — ELIAS SPECTOR (father; Rabbi; Holocaust survivor; deceased)

**Position in the file.** Load-bearing. Every other relationship the subject has ever entered is a reaction to, or a flight from, the figure of Elias.

**Biographical reconstruction.** Born interwar Europe; survived the camps (run-specific: Auschwitz in some flashbacks, unspecified in others); emigrated to the United States in the late 1940s; settled in Chicago; took a congregation in a working-class Jewish neighborhood. Married late. Scholarly, soft-spoken, observant, pacifist by conviction *after* the war rather than before it — meaning Marc grew up with a father whose gentleness was not naïveté but *chosen* in the teeth of demonstrated evil. The boy could not parse the choice as anything but weakness.

**Trust register.** Inverted. The subject trusted Elias *absolutely* on the small things — that the father would not lie, would not strike him, would not abandon him — and *not at all* on the load-bearing one: that the father could protect him, or anyone, from the world Elias had himself barely escaped. Trust in competence was zero by age eight. Trust in love was total, and intolerable.

**Behavioral evidence in the subject's adult life.**
- He cannot tolerate a male authority figure who declines to use force. Pacifist clergy, ACLU lawyers, the unarmed scholar archetype — he treats them with elaborate, performative courtesy that masks a contempt he himself does not name.
- Conversely, he is incapable of refusing a male authority figure who *does* use force and who claims a moral frame. Bushman, the early CIA handlers, Khonshu — each occupies the negative-print of Elias.
- He observes Jewish practice in fragments: lights yahrzeit candles, knows the Mourner's Kaddish from memory, will not eat pork in front of Frenchie, kept a tallit in a footlocker through three apartment moves (Lemire interior). He does not attend synagogue. The fragments are addressed *to Elias,* not to God. They are letters that cannot be delivered.
- He cannot bear to be called *rabbi's son* by an enemy. Antagonists who learn the biographical detail and weaponize it (Sun King; certain Bushman-affiliated figures) reliably draw a disproportionate, undisciplined response. The phrase reaches a place no tactical training has reached.

**Childhood dynamic.** Reconstructible from Lemire's flashbacks and the Bemis institutional sequences. The boy Marc:
- Asked Elias questions about the camps and was answered, gently, with parables rather than facts. He read the parables as evasion.
- Brought home injuries from schoolyard fights and was met not with punishment but with grief — Elias would touch the bruise and say nothing. The subject still cannot tolerate being looked at with grief; he will leave the room.
- Was taken to shul and seated beside his father; was told he had a beautiful voice; refused to sing.
- Once (Lemire #5, flashback) saw Elias decline to defend himself from a street antisemite, walking past with eyes lowered. The boy went back the next day alone and bloodied the man with a rock. He did not tell Elias. This is the subject's *first deliberate act of proxy violence on behalf of a parent who would not perform it himself* — the operational template of the entire vigilante career, present at age ten or eleven.

**Adolescent and adult dynamic.** Marc left home as soon as legally able. He went to boxing first (a structured way to be hit and to hit back, with rules his father could not endorse but also could not forbid), then enlisted — both choices calculated to be *the opposite of Elias*. Contact during the Marines and CIA years was minimal: postcards, the occasional phone call on the High Holy Days. Elias, by all available evidence, never reproached him, which the subject experienced as a further species of weakness and a further species of love, indistinguishable.

**The death of Elias.** Per the Lemire run and corroborated in MacKay, Elias died while Marc was overseas (mercenary period). Marc did not return for the funeral; in some accounts, he did not learn of the death for weeks. The unmourned father is one of the deep sources of the subject's relationship to death generally — he cannot perform standard grief rituals because he failed to perform the first one. Each subsequent death he witnesses (Marlene's father; the archaeologists at the dig; allies in the field) is partially *Elias's funeral*, which is why his responses are inappropriate to the occasion: too violent, too detached, or too late.

**The post-mortem dynamic — which is the real dynamic.** Elias is more present to the subject dead than he ever was alive. The Khonshu apparatus can be read, with very little strain, as an elaborate inversion-effigy of the father: a desert god instead of a desert-people's God; a deity who *demands* killing instead of one who forbids it; a voice in the head where Elias's voice was a touch on the bruise. The subject prays to Khonshu in the cadence of liturgical Hebrew (verified across Lemire and MacKay scripting). He has built a parallel religion whose entire purpose is to refute the one his father transmitted, and the refutation requires the original to remain intact in memory. He cannot let Elias go because Elias is the *thing being argued against*.

**Failure mode.** Any environment that forces the subject to confront Elias's actual moral position — that violence, even righteous violence, does not heal and may compound the wound — produces either flight (alter-switch, usually to Jake, who has no patience for theology) or collapse (depressive immobility lasting days). The Lemire asylum arc is in part an extended forced encounter with a therapist-figure who occupies the Elias-position; the subject's near-catatonia is legible as the original childhood paralysis reactivated.

**Leverage (analytic, not operational).** To approach the subject through Elias is to approach his deepest unintegrated material. It is the most powerful and the most dangerous lever: powerful because it bypasses every defense; dangerous because the defenses exist for a reason and dismantling them without scaffolding produces decompensation, not integration. Any therapeutic, diplomatic, or coercive use of the Elias material must be prepared to hold the subject through a multi-day acute episode. The MacKay-era Midnight Mission represents the first environment in the subject's adult life capable of holding such an episode without him fleeing or dying; it is therefore also the first environment in which Elias has become *speakable* in his presence. Track this.

---

### 6.2 — WENDY SPECTOR (mother; status: deceased; access to memory: heavily defended)

**Position in the file.** The dissociated parent. For nearly four decades of publication history Wendy was a near-absence — mentioned, implied, not drawn. The Bemis run and MacKay flashbacks have since established her as the abusive parent the subject spent his childhood splitting off in order to preserve his love for Elias. This is now the most credible etiological substrate for the DID, and supersedes the Khonshu-origin reading of the alters.

**Reconstructed biography.** Married Elias; bore at least one son (Marc); declined across the subject's childhood into a mental illness that was never named, treated, or, within the household, openly acknowledged. Episodes of violence and verbal cruelty alternated with periods of withdrawal. Elias managed her with the same pacific patience he applied to everything, which from the boy's vantage was a second failure of protection compounding the first.

**Dynamic, childhood.** The data points, assembled from flashbacks across Bemis and MacKay:
- The mother who screams in a closed room and the mother who tucks the child into bed are remembered as *different people*. This is the genesis fact of the dissociative structure. Before there were Steven and Jake, there were two Wendys, and the boy who could not reconcile them learned the trick of letting one self meet one mother and another self meet the other.
- Physical punishment that exceeded any disciplinary frame — implements, duration, locations on the body easily covered by clothing. The subject's adult somatic indifference to pain dates here, not to the Marines.
- Verbal content: accusations that the boy was responsible for the mother's state; that he was unloved by God; that he was "wrong" in ways unspecified. The subject's adult conviction of his own foundational badness — *I am not a good man* — is in her cadence, not his own.
- Elias did not intervene. Whether by incapacity, theology, or his own dissociation of the marriage is not knowable. The boy registered the non-intervention as complicity, then split *that* perception off as well, because to hold it would be to lose both parents at once.

**The construction of Steven Grant.** Best read as the earliest alter, formed in childhood as the *boy the mother could not reach.* Steven is uninjured, well-mannered, financially secure, socially fluent — every quality the bruised observant boy was not. Steven does not remember the mother. The subject's adult Steven-states show flickers of confusion when maternal material is raised; the alter has no apparatus for it.

**The construction of Jake Lockley.** Plausibly later (latency or early adolescence), formed as *the boy who would not be hit again.* Jake speaks in working-class registers the Spector household did not use, moves through the street the way Elias did not, and has access to anger Marc-self could not safely hold inside the home. Jake also has no maternal memory — but where Steven's blankness is genteel, Jake's is contemptuous; ask Jake about his mother and you get an obscenity and a closed door.

**Adult dynamic.** The subject did not, by any available evidence, visit Wendy in her final illness or attend her funeral. He is reported, in a single Bemis interior, to have learned of her death by mail, read the letter twice, and burned it. He has never, in canon, spoken her name aloud to another character without prompting. Marlene has asked twice across the decades; Frenchie, never; the MacKay-era therapeutic figures have approached the topic obliquely and been deflected.

**Behavioral evidence in the subject's adult life.**
- Women who present as fragile-and-volatile activate an unusually intense protective response *and* an unusually intense urge to flee. He cannot stay in a room with a woman crying behind a closed door; he will either break the door or leave the building.
- He is exceptionally tender with women who have been beaten by men, and exceptionally cold with women who have beaten their own children. The latter he has killed (off-panel implications, Huston-era), in conditions where his stated operational code would have permitted restraint.
- He sleeps badly with a woman in the bed. Marlene reports (Moench-era, oblique) that he wakes at the sound of her breath changing. The hypervigilance reads as combat-conditioned and is — but the substrate is older.
- He has never sought a maternal figure as a confidante. Gena Landers (the diner owner) is the closest he has come, and the relationship is carefully structured to prevent intimacy: he pays for coffee, she feeds him, the transaction holds the bond at a safe distance.

**Failure mode.** The Wendy material, unlike the Elias material, is not yet *speakable* even within the Midnight Mission frame. The subject can grieve Elias in fragments; he cannot grieve Wendy at all, because to grieve her would require first to *have* her as a coherent figure, and the dissociative architecture exists precisely to prevent her coherence. Any forced integration of the maternal memory risks not therapeutic breakthrough but the collapse of the alter-system that has organized his functioning life. Steven and Jake are, among other things, the boys who agreed never to know her. Dissolve them and you will dissolve the agreement.

**Leverage.** Approach with extreme caution and only in containment. A clinically informed antagonist who learned to speak in Wendy's cadence — the particular alternation of caress and accusation — could destabilize the subject more rapidly than any physical threat. There is no current evidence that any enemy possesses this knowledge. The Sun King figure (Bemis) approached it intuitively; the Sun King's lethality to the subject's psyche was disproportionate to his actual capability for this reason.

---

### 6.3 — RANDALL SPECTOR (brother; status: ambiguous — possibly delusional, possibly real, certainly murderous)

**Position in the file.** The shadow-sibling. The fact that Randall's *ontological status* has been retconned across runs (real brother in Moench; dissociative production in Bemis; recomplicated in MacKay) is, for intelligence purposes, the most important thing about him. Whether or not a Randall ever drew breath, *the subject required* a Randall, and produced one when reality did not supply him.

**The Moench account.** Older brother (or younger, run-dependent); developed early psychopathy; killed a girl in adolescence; institutionalized; escaped; resurfaces in the subject's adult life as the costumed killer **Hatchet-Man** / **Shadowknight**, repeatedly. The Moench-era Randall is a clean externalization of everything the subject fears he is at base: a Spector who let the violence have him, with no Khonshu and no white costume to dress it in service.

**The Bemis recomplication.** Randall is reframed, in part, as a delusional production — a brother the subject manufactured to hold the unbearable knowledge that *he himself* did certain things in childhood and adolescence. This reading is psychiatrically coherent (alter-attribution of forbidden acts is well-documented in DID) and narratively destabilizing in exactly the way the subject's own memory is destabilizing.

**For intelligence purposes, assume both are partly true.** There was likely a brother; the brother likely did harm; the subject likely *also* attributed his own dissociated harms to that brother across decades, until brother-as-person and brother-as-receptacle became inseparable. Operationally treat Randall as a *real figure with a hypertrophied symbolic function.*

**Childhood dynamic, reconstructed.**
- Two boys in the Wendy/Elias household, splitting the impossible parental field between them. If Randall existed, he absorbed material Marc could not (and vice versa). Sibling rivalry, in this house, was not for parental attention but for *which of the available bad outcomes one would carry.*
- The girl Randall killed (Moench) — the subject witnessed or discovered or was told; the precise position is murky and the murkiness is itself a sign of dissociative encoding. The subject's adult ferocity in defense of girls and young women is over-explained by Wendy alone; the Randall-victim layer is the additional charge.
- The institutional confinement of Randall planted the seed of the subject's lifelong horror of psychiatric facilities — a horror that has *not* prevented his own repeated confinement, because horror and compulsion-toward operate in him as a single circuit.

**Adult dynamic.** Each Randall reappearance follows a pattern:
1. Randall surfaces in costume, having harmed or threatened a woman or child.
2. The subject engages with disproportionate emotional charge — fights longer than tactical, takes injuries he would not take from a comparable threat, refuses backup.
3. The subject does not, ultimately, kill Randall, though he has killed lesser men for lesser offenses. The brother is the one antagonist whose execution would be an execution of self.
4. Randall escapes or is institutionalized; the subject does not visit him; the cycle resets.

**The not-killing is diagnostic.** Marc Spector kills. He has killed many men in white. He does not kill his brother. Whatever Randall is — sibling, delusion, externalized alter, all three — he is the one figure outside Khonshu whom the subject treats as *kin in the operational sense*: bound by something prior to the moral frame.

**Trust register.** Zero. Randall has betrayed every truce, broken every confinement, returned to harm. The subject does not trust him and continues, against all evidence, to engage him as if trust were retrievable. This is the *sibling* relational template — not friendship, not alliance, but the prior bond that survives demonstrated unworthiness because severing it would sever something in the self.

**Behavioral evidence in the subject's adult life.**
- Mirror antagonists destabilize him categorically. The Sun King (Bemis), Bushman's heirs, any costumed figure whose costume *quotes* his — these draw responses out of proportion to threat. He is fighting Randall by other names.
- He cannot maintain a partnership with a male peer who shares his methods without it deteriorating. The Avengers tenures (West Coast, Secret Avengers) all sour. Hunter's Moon / Dr. Badr (MacKay), introduced as a *sane* counter-avatar, is the first attempted male peer relationship structured deliberately as *not-Randall*; its stability is therefore the most important data point in the subject's late-period relational record. Watch this relationship; its degradation would signal a serious regression.
- He is unable to mentor young men without converting the relationship into a covert competition.

**Failure mode.** Any operation involving Randall, or a figure the subject reads as a Randall-equivalent, defeats his tactical discipline. He will accept casualties, including his own, rather than disengage. He will refuse the killing shot at the moment it is offered and pay for the refusal in subsequent civilian harm. Predictable across forty years.

**Leverage.** The brother is a lever for *engagement,* not for control — surface a credible Randall and the subject will appear, on schedule, undefended. He is the bait that has never failed.

---

### 6.4 — THE UNNAMED CHILDREN OF THE SUBJECT

**Position in the file.** Negative space. The subject has no biological children of record. The absence is *active*, not incidental, and must be treated as a relationship in its own right.

**Behavioral evidence.**
- He has, across decades, declined every implicit and several explicit offers of fatherhood from Marlene. The refusals are couched as practical (the danger of his life) but Marlene-interiors across Moench and Huston make clear she experienced them as constitutional.
- He cannot hold an infant on panel without the artist drawing him stiff. (Verifiable: every infant-holding scene from Moench forward shows the same locked elbows, the same averted gaze.)
- He is, by contrast, exceptionally fluent with children old enough to speak. He kneels to their height (a consistent body-language tell across writers and artists); he answers their questions literally rather than performatively; he does not lie to them about the danger they are in. Children, in turn, trust him on first contact more reliably than adults do — a phenomenon the MacKay run foregrounds with the Mission's regular intake of frightened minors.

**The structural reading.** The subject cannot father because to father would be to risk constructing another Elias-Marc dyad with himself in the Elias role, or another Wendy-Marc dyad with himself in the Wendy role. He does not know which he would become and cannot tolerate the uncertainty. The non-fathering is therefore *protective* — of the unborn child, of Marlene, and of the parents in him who would not survive the test. It is one of the few decisions in his life that is, on examination, unambiguously moral.

**The displaced fathering.** What he cannot do as a father he performs as a guardian — the Midnight Mission's child cases, the recurrent rescue of trafficked minors across the MacKay run, the protective adoption of Gena's sons in the Moench-era diner scenes (he taught one of them to box; he attended the other's bar mitzvah, in costume, from the back of the room). These are the children of the file. They number perhaps a dozen across the canon. He remembers all of their names. Marlene reports (oblique, Huston) that he keeps a list.

**Leverage.** The list. Threats to any name on it override every other operational priority. There is no countervailing consideration. This is the most reliable predictor of his movement in the file.

---

### 6.5 — THE ANCESTORS / THE SIX MILLION

**Position in the file.** Background radiation. Not a relationship in the conventional sense, but a constant inherited pressure that shapes every other family bond and cannot be omitted from a complete map.

**The transmission.** Elias did not speak of the camps in detail but lived in their aftermath visibly — a thinness, a particular silence at certain dates on the calendar, a refusal of certain foods, a way of folding clothes. The subject absorbed the survival as ambient information before he had a frame for it. By adolescence he had constructed his own private theology of the inheritance: that he had been born owing a debt, that the debt was payable only in protection of the targeted, and that his father's pacifist version of the debt-payment was insufficient. The mercenary years are the debt mis-paid (violence for hire, against any target); the Khonshu years are the debt re-paid (violence in service, against predators of the helpless). The arithmetic is his, not Elias's; Elias would have rejected it.

**Behavioral evidence.**
- He has, on multiple occasions, intervened in antisemitic violence with a ferocity that exceeds his already-high baseline. The Skinhead arc (Dixon-era); a Brooklyn incident in Lemire; a desecrated cemetery in MacKay. In each, the costume is incidental; the response is *Marc's*, not Khonshu's.
- He fasts on Yom Kippur even when operationally inadvisable. Frenchie has, on at least one verified occasion, refused a mission for this reason on his behalf.
- He knows, and has been heard reciting under his breath in moments of acute stress, the names of relatives killed in the Shoah. The list is short — six names, per the Lemire interior — and the recitation functions as a self-locating prayer when dissociation threatens. It is, notably, the *one* litany he speaks that is neither Khonshu's nor his own self-condemnation.

**Failure mode.** Any attempt to construe his work as untethered from this inheritance — to read him as a generic costumed operator, or as a purely Egyptian-mythological figure — produces in him a quiet, durable contempt that he does not announce but that informs every subsequent interaction with the misreader. Several alliances have failed at this seam without the other party understanding why.

**Leverage.** None safely usable. The inheritance is the one part of him that is *not* dissociated, *not* fragmented, and *not* available for manipulation. It is, paradoxically, the healthiest structure in the file. Any attempt to weaponize it would be detected and would terminate the relationship with the attempter, permanently.

---

### 6.6 — KHONSHU (functional family member; classification: surrogate father / abusive spouse / dissociated persecutor-protector introject — pick one or all)

**Position in the file.** Included in this section, not in Section 7 (Allies & Operational Bonds), because the relational structure is *familial,* not professional. Khonshu does not employ the subject; Khonshu *raised* him, in the sense that the subject's adult self was finalized in Khonshu's tomb. Every category that applies to a parent applies here.

**The subst


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# UATU ANALYSIS FILE: MARC SPECTOR / MOON KNIGHT
## Section 6 — Relationships II: Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

A preliminary note on methodology. Subject's intimate-pair attachments (Marlene Alraune; the wife-of-record from the MacKay run; the various entanglements with operatives and clinicians who crossed the line into romance) are filed separately under Relationships I. This section maps the *operational* circle — the people he has chosen to keep, brought into the work, taught, learned from, and bled with, who are not lovers and not enemies. The pattern across fifty years of file material is consistent and worth foregrounding before the entries: subject's chosen family is **small, geographically fixed, functionally specialized, and never permitted to overlap roles**. Each person holds one keyed function (logistics, intelligence, conscience, succession), and subject organizes his life so that no single member ever sees more than a slice of him. The dossier reads, in aggregate, like a compartmentalized intelligence cell — which is exactly what it is, and exactly what his dissociative architecture requires.

---

### 6.1 — Jean-Paul "Frenchie" DuChamp

**History.** First documented association predates the Sudan event (MK vol.1 #1 retro flashbacks; expanded in Moench backups and again in the Huston run). DuChamp, French national, ex–Foreign Legion pilot, served alongside subject in mercenary contracts across North and East Africa through the mid-late 1970s. Present in Bushman's employ at the dig massacre; departs with subject; co-witnesses the desert death and the temple resurrection. From that moment forward DuChamp is the **only continuously-present human across every era of subject's adult life** — Moench, Dixon, Huston (where DuChamp loses a leg to a car bomb meant for subject), Bendis (estranged), Ellis (off-stage, alluded to), Lemire (a fixed point in subject's memory verification), MacKay (re-integrated as a Mission ally).

**Operational dynamic.** Pilot, getaway driver, weapons sourcing, secondary tactician. The Mooncopter and every successor aircraft are his domain; subject does not fly. DuChamp is also the **only person besides Marlene with continuous knowledge of all three original alters as alters** — i.e., he knows when "Steven" is on the phone and when "Jake" is in the cab, and adjusts his behavior without forcing the switch back. This unobtrusive accommodation is a load-bearing element of subject's stability; he does not have to perform coherence for DuChamp.

**Trust and safety rating.** *Maximal.* Of any human being on file, DuChamp is the one subject does not surveil, does not lie to about operational matters, and does not test. The single point of friction in their long history — DuChamp's eventual coming-out as a gay man, and the prior years of unrequited romantic attachment to subject which DuChamp disclosed in the Huston era — was metabolized without rupture. Subject's response, on file, is characteristic: blunt acknowledgment, no withdrawal, no overcorrection. (This is one of the few documented instances of subject *receiving* a difficult disclosure without retreating into an alter.)

**Failure mode.** DuChamp is the person subject will get killed by *using too long.* The bombing that took his leg is the file's central exhibit: DuChamp was targeted because of his proximity to subject, and subject responded with months of self-laceration that read, in retrospect, as proof that he had organized the relationship around the assumption DuChamp would always survive whatever subject's enemies sent. The pattern recurs in lower-stakes form across decades: subject calls DuChamp into operations where DuChamp's age, prosthetic, and non-enhanced status make him the weakest field asset, because subject *cannot conceive* of an operation without him.

**Leverage.** Anyone seeking to move subject moves DuChamp. The file lists DuChamp as the highest-priority third-party protection requirement in any assessment of subject's environment. A credible threat to DuChamp will produce a tactical response from subject that bypasses every other consideration including the Mission's standing rules of engagement. Inversely, DuChamp is the only person in the file with the demonstrated standing to talk subject *down* from a Khonshu-driven escalation — not by argument (which fails) but by refusing to fly the mission. The grounding of the aircraft is, historically, the only veto on the avatar that has ever worked.

---

### 6.2 — Gena Landers

**History.** Proprietor of a diner in subject's preferred Manhattan operational sector (originally the Bronx / upper-Manhattan margin in Moench; floats across boroughs in later runs). Introduced in the original solo run as the Jake Lockley persona's primary HUMINT node. Widow, two sons (Ray and Ricky, both watched grow up across the runs), Black, working-class, lived through more of New York than subject ever will.

**Operational dynamic.** Gena is the Jake-alter's anchor and his moral floor. Jake comes in, eats, listens, picks up street rumor — pimps moving, dealers shifting territory, missing girls, abusive husbands — and Gena passes it to him in the matter-of-fact register of a woman who has seen the neighborhood swallow people and is keeping a private ledger. She is not an informant in the tradecraft sense; she is a *neighbor* who has decided to use a strange man with a cab as her ledger's enforcement arm. This distinction matters: Jake-alter does work *for Gena* as much as Gena works *for Jake.*

**Trust and safety rating.** *High, but compartmentalized.* Gena knows Jake. Gena does not know Marc. Across multiple runs the file shows subject deliberately preserving this compartment — when out of cab and into white, he routes around her diner; when crises require Steven Grant's resources, he does not bring them through her. She has met "Marc" perhaps three times in fifty years of association and on at least two of those occasions did not recognize him. This is not a failure of intimacy on her part; it is subject's design.

**Failure mode.** Subject has twice (Moench; MacKay) gotten Gena's sons into proximity of danger that should have killed them. Ricky in particular has been targeted by Committee remnants and by later antagonists who reverse-engineered Jake's information network. Subject's response pattern is to *intensify* the protection while *refusing* to terminate the relationship — he will not give up Gena because Gena is the one place Jake can sit down and be addressed as a person, and Jake without Gena collapses into pure street-violence affect with no off-switch.

**Leverage.** Threats to Ray and Ricky move subject more reliably than threats to almost any other figure including, in some documented instances, Marlene. The reason is structural: harm to children is the file's confirmed override condition (see §3, drive 2), and Gena's sons have been *children in subject's protection* for so long that even as adults they retain the categorical flag. Anyone with knowledge of Gena's existence and standing should be considered to hold a primary lever on Jake-alter specifically and through Jake on the whole subject.

---

### 6.3 — Khonshu (entered here under protest of category)

**History.** Filed under Mentors because the operational reality is that Khonshu functions as one regardless of ontological status. Whether Khonshu is (a) an extant Ennead deity, (b) a dissociated persecutor/protector introject organized around the Sudan death-event, (c) a CTE-potentiated hallucination structured by the iconography subject collapsed in front of, or (d) some braided composite of all three — the **behavioral output is the same**: a demanding senior voice that issues mission tasking, withholds and grants approval, punishes refusal with somatic and psychiatric symptoms, and supplies the only continuous narrative thread across subject's adult life. The dossier treats it operationally as a relationship.

**Dynamic.** Abusive-mentor pattern with high textbook fidelity: intermittent reinforcement; isolation of subject from competing frames (every era shows Khonshu undermining subject's outside attachments — Marlene, the Avengers, the Mission); narrative monopoly ("I brought you back; you are mine"); escalation of demands during periods of subject's stability; withdrawal during periods of subject's collapse, which subject then experiences as abandonment and works to recover. Subject's compliance is not principled — he openly hates Khonshu in multiple eras (Huston explicitly; MacKay implicitly through ministry-as-alternative) — but is structural. He cannot stop because the relationship is the organizing axis of the personality.

**Trust and safety rating.** *Adversarial-codependent.* Khonshu lies to subject; subject knows Khonshu lies to subject; subject obeys anyway because the obedience produces the only state in which subject feels coherent. The Lemire arc is the file's clearest demonstration: offered a frame in which Khonshu does not exist, subject cannot retain it, *not because the frame is implausible but because subject cannot live inside it.*

**Failure mode.** Catastrophic. Every era has at least one operation in which Khonshu's tasking is morally indefensible and subject executes it, then spends the subsequent issues paying for it. The Huston scalping; the Bendis-era LA assaults; the late-MacKay confrontations. Khonshu is the in-house source of subject's worst acts.

**Leverage.** Inverted. *Khonshu is the lever others pull on subject;* there is no lever on Khonshu that subject controls. The only documented disruptions of the channel are (i) Hunter's Moon's parallel avatar status, which provides a comparison case subject can use to bracket Khonshu's demands, and (ii) the Mission framework, which reroutes Khonshu's tasking through subject's own triage rather than accepting it directly. Both are mitigations, not severances.

---

### 6.4 — Dr. Peter Alraune (posthumous mentor)

**History.** The archaeologist whose dig Bushman massacred in Sudan; Marlene's father; the man whose death subject failed to prevent. Subject knew him for hours, possibly a day. He has remained a fixed figure in subject's interior cosmology for fifty publication years.

**Dynamic.** Alraune is the **scholar-father subject failed,** a near-perfect substitute for Elias Spector. The Sudan event is structurally a repetition: a gentle, learned man dies because subject was inadequate to protect him, and subject's response is to construct a life that retroactively justifies the protection that arrived too late. Every Khonshu-tomb artifact subject preserves, every academic consultation he funds via the Steven Grant identity, every museum-piece return he has engineered traces back to Alraune as the unspoken honoree.

**Trust / failure / leverage.** Not applicable in the usual sense; Alraune is a dead man whose function in subject's psychology is to remain dead and remain owed. The leverage operates in reverse: *invocation of Alraune's memory* in negotiation with subject — by Marlene, historically; by antagonists who have done the research, rarely — produces a guilt response that overrides tactical judgment. The dossier flags this as a Marlene-class vulnerability.

---

### 6.5 — Reese (cat) and other small dependents

**History.** The cat first appears in the Bemis era and recurs through MacKay. Subordinate to the file's larger pattern: subject reliably accretes small, voiceless dependents during periods of decompensation — the cat; the safe-house pigeons; in MacKay, the rotating cast of Mission patients with no other shelter.

**Dynamic.** The dependents do not require coherence. They do not ask which alter is feeding them. They consume care without demanding integration. This is the only relational configuration in which subject can give without cost.

**Failure mode.** When the dependents are threatened, subject's response is disproportionate by an order of magnitude that even DuChamp finds excessive. When subject loses one — and across runs he has lost several — the loss reads in his behavior for months.

**Leverage.** Low individually, high in aggregate. An adversary who understood the pattern would not target Reese; they would *remove the entire dependent stratum* (clear the Mission, scatter the patients) and watch subject lose the regulation system that the daily caretaking provides.

---

### 6.6 — Dr. Badr / Hunter's Moon

**History.** Introduced in the MacKay run as a parallel avatar of Khonshu, sane where subject is fractured, integrated where subject is distributed, an Egyptian-trained physician who carries Khonshu's mandate alongside a functioning medical practice and a stable identity.

**Dynamic.** Hunter's Moon is the **succession plan and the diagnostic mirror.** His existence resolves a fifty-year question — *is the dysfunction Khonshu's fault or Marc's?* — by demonstrating that another person can hold the same channel without the same damage. Subject's response to Badr cycles, in the available file, through (i) initial hostility (the mirror provokes mirror-violence per §5 pressure points), (ii) grudging operational cooperation, (iii) something like a younger-brother register that subject has not displayed since the Randall material, and (iv) — most importantly — a willingness to designate Badr as continuity. The MacKay-era death sequence is comprehensible only if read as subject preparing the post-Marc Khonshu-avatar structure.

**Trust and safety rating.** *Conditionally high and rising.* Badr is the rare ally subject does not have to protect *from* the work; Badr came in already inside it.

**Failure mode.** The mirror function cuts both ways. If Badr fails morally, subject loses the proof-of-concept that the channel can be held cleanly, and the Khonshu-blame defense collapses back onto subject. If Badr succeeds beyond subject, subject's investment in being *necessary* is undermined and the depressive substrate resurfaces.

**Leverage.** Moderate. Badr's medical credentialing and institutional access make him visible in ways subject is not; an antagonist could attack subject through Badr's professional standing rather than his body, an attack vector subject is poorly equipped to defend.

---

### 6.7 — Soldier, Tigra, and the Avengers tenure (West Coast era and after)

**History.** Subject's documented Avengers affiliations span the Dixon-era West Coast roster, the Bendis-era Secret Avengers / *Vengeance* period, and intermittent later call-ups. He is, on paper, a peer of capes who have known each other for decades.

**Dynamic.** Subject is **institutionally unassimilable.** Every team tenure shows the same arc: recruited for capability, valued in the field, distrusted in the briefing room, eventually self-extruded. The friction sources are predictable from the personality file — Steven-alter's wealth-class register grates on team-mates of different backgrounds; Jake-alter's methods violate sanctioned rules of engagement; Marc-self's Khonshu-tasking does not coordinate with team mission planning; and subject's inability to share interior life produces a recurring perception that he is *running side operations the team is not read into,* which is usually accurate.

**Trust and safety rating.** *Tactical mid; relational low.* Specific peers — Tigra in the West Coast period; the Defenders-spectrum allies who have worked with him in supernatural matters — have functional working trust. Iron Man / SHRA-era institutional capes effectively never; subject's reading of authority figures patterns onto them and the relationships do not stabilize.

**Failure mode.** The Bendis-era hallucinated-Avengers material is the file's clearest evidence: subject *cannot situate himself as a peer to canonical heroes,* and when forced to operate in their register he generates them as internal alters rather than relate to them externally. The team-affiliation pattern is therefore an unstable stress configuration for him, not a resource.

**Leverage.** Limited. The peers do not have standing to move him; they have standing to embarrass him institutionally, which he tolerates without behavior change.

---

### 6.8 — The Midnight Mission patients (collective)

**History.** The MacKay-era development: subject opens a storefront in Manhattan offering protection and triage to people whose problems fall in the seam between psychiatry, occult affliction, and street violence. The intake is continuous and the population rotates.

**Dynamic.** The patients are the **first relational structure in subject's life that uses his pathology adaptively.** Each intake is a person whose experience subject is uniquely qualified to credit — the dissociative, the haunted, the religiously violated, the people other clinicians cannot hear. Subject does not have to translate; the patients arrive already speaking his dialect. This is also the first context in which subject's identity as Elias Spector's son operates *as competence* rather than as injury — the rabbinical inheritance, the pastoral instinct, the obligation to the stranger and the broken, all of which subject has previously enacted in mute violent form, here become legible as ministry.

**Trust and safety rating.** *Calibrated low individual, high aggregate.* Subject does not over-invest in single patients (the dependent stratum, §6.5, absorbs that drive); he invests in the institution.

**Failure mode.** The Mission is the first thing subject has built whose loss would be a categorical defeat. Prior losses (Marlene partings, team exits, even Sudan) were survivable inside the existing fragmentation. The Mission *is* the integration vehicle; if it is destroyed and cannot be rebuilt, subject loses the only adaptive sublimation in the file. Threats to the Mission are therefore threats to subject's late-life psychological organization, not merely to a workplace.

**Leverage.** High and underexploited in the historical record. Antagonists have so far attacked the Mission as a tactical asset; the file's assessment is that an antagonist who attacked it as a *symbolic* asset — discrediting it, turning a patient against it, exposing its irregular methods to institutional psychiatry — would do more damage than any direct assault.

---

### 6.9 — Crawley (street informant)

**History.** Bowery-class informant from the Moench run; recurring across decades in cameo. An alcoholic former Shakespearean (the file's term, not entirely facetious) who trades information for cash and dignity. Jake-alter's secondary HUMINT node after Gena.

**Dynamic.** Crawley is the **member of the chosen circle subject is most like and least able to acknowledge being like.** A man whose identity has fractured under pressure (the lost theatrical career, the alcohol, the street years), who survives by performing personae for paying audiences — the parallel is unsubtle. Subject treats Crawley with a courtesy that exceeds the transactional baseline by a wide margin: pays above market, intervenes in his medical crises, has been documented retrieving him from holding cells under the Steven Grant identity's legal cover.

**Trust and safety rating.** *Functional working trust within compartment.* Crawley does not know subject's other identities and is not asked to. The relationship runs on the Jake channel exclusively.
