The decades of dissociation taught it earlier: he cannot control which of himself is currently driving. He has internalized this as an *operational discipline* rather than a despair. The discipline runs as follows:

- **Control the small radius absolutely.** His immediate body, his immediate gear, his immediate sightlines. The pre-mission rituals (weapons check, cape arrangement, the particular order in which he dons the wraps — observed consistently across Huston, Ellis, MacKay) are not superstition; they are the available frontier of control and he occupies all of it.
- **Control the people you can keep alive.** He micromanages the safety of his small chosen cast to the edge of insult — Frenchie's flight routes, Marlene's apartment locks, the Mission staff's commute. He does not micromanage their *choices,* which he considers off-limits, but their *exposure* he treats as a personal responsibility he can never delegate.
- **Surrender the rest to Khonshu, and let Khonshu's demands be the ceiling of your responsibility.** This is the genius and the cage of the Khonshu arrangement. By outsourcing the moral horizon to a god he did not choose, he is freed from the unbearable burden of having chosen the work himself. Take Khonshu away (Ellis's late arc, Lemire's asylum, MacKay's death sequence) and the question *why am I doing this* returns with a force that nearly destroys him. He needs the god the way some men need the orders.
- **Refuse to be controlled by men.** He has a near-absolute allergy to *human* authority. The CIA betrayed him; the Marine command was an instrument he served and outgrew; the Avengers' chain-of-command he tolerates only when the work aligns. He will take orders from a god he is unsure exists more readily than from a man he can verify. The logic is consistent with his attachment template — gods can be hated and obeyed; men can only be hated.

He believes **other people's control of him is the deepest violation.** This is why imprisonment and institutionalization break him faster than torture does. Bushman could beat him to near-death and Marc came back; the asylum reduced him to a shape on a cot. He understands this about himself and considers it a vulnerability; he does not permit it to be exploited if he can see it coming.

---

### 6.5 Theory of Trust

Trust, in his operational code, is a **graduated and asymmetric** instrument. He extends it in tiers and never confuses the tiers.

- **Tier 0 — the small chosen.** Marlene, Frenchie, Gena and her sons in the Moench/Huston era; Reese, Soldier, Tigra-era allies; the Mission cohort under MacKay. These get his life. They do not get his interior. The arrangement is: I will die for you, you will not be asked to understand me. The asymmetry is the price he charges for the loyalty.
- **Tier 1 — operational allies in good standing.** Avengers in their West Coast era, Defenders, MacKay-era street-level peers. These get coordination, intelligence, backup. They do not get his real address, his real schedule, or the names of his alters in their full register.
- **Tier 2 — clients, informants, casework civilians.** These get his protection and a particular kind of fierce attention — he is gentler with them than with anyone above this tier, because they have asked for nothing and he is determined to give them what they need. He famously remembers names of children he has met once.
- **Tier 3 — institutions.** Hospitals, police, intelligence agencies. He treats them as weather. Sometimes they help, sometimes they harm, and the difference is largely outside his influence; he routes around them when he can and uses them when he must.
- **Tier 4 — peers in mask.** He distrusts other vigilantes by default until they prove a particular thing: that they will *stop.* He has watched too many costumed men cross the line he polices in himself; he reserves judgment.
- **Tier 5 — the predator class.** No trust under any circumstances. Surrender accepted, parole rejected. He does not believe in their rehabilitation and his record bears him out more than it should.

He **does not trust himself**, and this is the keystone. The dissociation has taught him that his perception, memory, and intentions are all corruptible by alters or by Khonshu or by his own mood. He has built compensations: writes things down (the journals are canon from Huston forward), cross-checks Steven's records against Jake's, makes Marlene a kind of audit function in earlier eras and the Mission staff in later ones. He treats himself as an *unreliable instrument operated under supervision,* and he is the supervisor. When the supervision fails — when alters override or Khonshu commandeers — he accepts the consequences as his own and does not blame the alter. This is one of the few moral disciplines that has held continuously across writers.

He believes **trust is built by witnessing,** not by disclosure. The people he loves most know him by what they have seen him do under fire, not by what he has told them about himself. He almost never tells them anything about himself. They have learned to read his silences and he considers this an acceptable substitute for confession.

---

### 6.6 Theory of Risk

Risk is the area where his philosophy is most thoroughly entangled with his pathology, and he knows it.

His operational risk calculus is **rigorous outward, reckless inward.** The cost of failure to a client, a child, an ally, or a civilian is weighted to near-infinity in his planning; the cost to himself is weighted at near-zero. This is not bravado. It is the consequence of three converging facts: (a) he genuinely values others' lives more than his own and considers that a moral achievement; (b) he expects to die in the work and has expected it since Sudan; (c) the *seeking* of risk is one of his subordinate drives — the punishment-craving channel of his death economy — and he uses operational necessity as legitimate cover for it.

He understands this third channel and tries to police it. The journals (Huston, Lemire, MacKay) contain repeated self-correction: *did I take that hit because I had to or because I wanted to.* The honest answer, often, is both. He has decided that as long as the operational necessity is real he will not deny himself the punishment that accompanies it, but he refuses to manufacture necessity for the sake of the punishment. The line is fragile and he has crossed it; the crossings are what the depressive episodes are made of.

His risk theory about **other people** is the opposite: he will pull a team back from a margin he would walk past himself. He will not let Frenchie fly a route he would fly alone. He will not let a Mission staffer answer a door he would answer. This asymmetry has caused friction with every team he has joined — peers experience it as condescension or as a refusal of solidarity, and they are not wrong, but they are not entirely right either. He cannot risk them because they are the *evidence* that the world contains people worth protecting; if he loses them he loses the cosmology.

He believes **the avoidance of risk is itself a moral failure** in his particular vocation. A Moon Knight who hedges is a Moon Knight who has chosen his own continuation over a victim's rescue. He will not be that. The willingness to be destroyed is, in his code, the entry fee — the thing that distinguishes the avenger from the bystander and from the predator alike. He suspects this is a rationalization for a death wish and he has decided he does not care, because the rationalization produces correct behavior in the field.

---

### 6.7 Theory of His Own Place

This is the section he would refuse to give if asked, so it must be reconstructed from behavior.

He believes he is **not a hero.** He uses the word for others — Captain America, the Mission's clients-turned-allies, occasionally Frenchie — and refuses it for himself with a consistency that has survived every writer's attempt to dislodge it. The refusal is not modesty. It is a precise category claim: heroes are men whose work flows from goodness, and his flows from debt. He is paying a bill, and the bill will not be cleared in his lifetime, and he does not expect it to be.

He believes he is **a particular kind of instrument** — sharpened by trauma, calibrated by Khonshu, aimed by a moral law inherited from a father he disappointed. He has stopped resenting this instrumentality and has begun, in the MacKay era, to find a strange dignity in it. The Midnight Mission is the first project in his life in which he has presented his fragmentation as an *offering* rather than a defect: *I am broken in these specific ways, and these specific breakages let me do work that whole men cannot.* He is right about this and he knows he is right and the knowing is the closest thing to peace he has had.

He believes he is **temporary.** He has died three times and expects a fourth. He has organized his affairs accordingly — successors trained (Hunter's Moon as the sane counter-avatar is acknowledged by him, with relief, as the man who can do the work without becoming the wreckage); the Mission staffed to outlast him; Marlene long ago freed from any expectation of his survival. He treats his life as a resource to be expended on schedule, and he considers the schedule a matter of mission tempo rather than self-preservation.

He believes he is **his father's son** and has stopped fighting the resemblance. Elias was a man who studied a moral law and tried to live inside it under conditions that should have made the law impossible. Marc has done the inverse — taken the moral law into conditions where only its violations are operative — and the symmetry is not lost on him. The Jewish identity that Lemire and MacKay foregrounded was always there; what changed is that he stopped treating it as the thing he had betrayed and started treating it as the thing he was, in his own crooked way, carrying. The rabbi's son works nights now. The Torah is still the Torah. The crescent is the tool the night requires.

He believes — and this is the operational secret of him — **that the work is worth more than the worker, and that the worker's incoherence is acceptable as long as the work is coherent.** He has, over fifty years of recorded behavior, refused every offer of integration that would have cost him the work, and accepted every cost to himself that the work has demanded. He calls this service. The literature calls it pathology. Both are accurate descriptions of the same arrangement, and the arrangement, on the evidence, has saved more lives than it has ended, including — repeatedly, against his expectation — his own.


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# UATU ANALYSIS FILE: MARC SPECTOR / MOON KNIGHT
## Section 6 — Moral & Ethical Framework

---

### 6.1 The Inherited Frame vs. the Enacted Code

To understand what Marc Spector will and will not do, one must first separate the two ethical systems running concurrently inside him, because his behavior is the friction between them.

The **inherited frame** is rabbinic Jewish ethics filtered through a Holocaust-survivor father: the sanctity of *pikuach nefesh* (the preservation of life overrides nearly all commandments), the prohibition against humiliating another person (*halbanat panim*), the duty to remember (*zakhor*), the conviction that justice is God's prerogative tempered by human responsibility (*tzedek tzedek tirdof*). Elias Spector's pacifism is not weakness; it is a *post-Auschwitz theological position* — the refusal to become what the world tried to make of Jews. Marc was raised inside this frame and *knows* it intimately. He can quote it. He invokes it (especially in the Lemire and MacKay runs) when grounding himself. It is the moral grammar he will never lose.

The **enacted code** is something else: a Khonshu-shaped operational ethics built from the inverted premise — that the world's evil is so present and so unrestrained that a Jew who refuses violence is now a Jew who watches the next murder happen. It is, in effect, Elias Spector's ethics read *against* Elias Spector, by a son who decided his father's gentleness was a luxury bought by other people's deaths.

Everything Marc actually does sits in the gap between the two. He is not a hypocrite. He is a man enforcing the inherited values *with* methods the inherited values forbid, and he knows it, and the guilt that knowledge generates is itself a load-bearing component of how he stays operational.

---

### 6.2 The Hard Lines (Things He Will Not Do)

These are remarkably stable from 1975 forward, across every writer. The man's prohibitions are firmer than his permissions.

**He will not harm a child, full stop.** Not as collateral, not under coercion, not in any moral-philosophy thought experiment. The single most reliable behavioral predictor in the file: a threatened child in the operational frame overrides every other consideration including tactical retreat, including the safety of named allies, including direct orders from Khonshu (the Huston run and MacKay run both depict moments where Marc *defies the god* on this axis). The protection of children is the only place his code is genuinely unconditional.

**He will not harm a victim's body further to extract information.** He will menace, restrain, terrify; he will not torture for intel from anyone he reads as already-prey. The torture instinct, when it appears, is reserved exclusively for confirmed predators (see 6.3) and is then *expressive* (punishment-ritual) rather than *instrumental* (interrogation).

**He will not abandon an asset in the field.** Frenchie's safety is non-negotiable across the entire Moench, Dixon, Huston, and MacKay runs. Gena and her sons receive the same protection. Reese, latterly. Even allies he distrusts (Tigra-era teammates, Avengers colleagues he doesn't like) get extraction priority over mission completion. This is the *one* place where the mercenary residue is wholly purged: the post-Sudan Marc does not leave men behind, because Sudan was the moment a man (himself) was left behind.

**He will not pretend to be sane to gain advantage with the vulnerable.** He discloses his condition to the broken (children, traumatized victims, the institutionalized) with a directness that startles them. The "I am crazy" admission is partly defense (see psychological assessment, §3), but at this register it functions ethically — he refuses to deceive someone already deceived by their own mind. He *will* deceive the strong, the institutional, the predatory, the Avengers when expedient. He will not deceive a frightened person about what he is.

**He will not work for money.** This is the cleanest line in the file and the one that defines the entire post-Sudan life. Steven Grant's fortune funds the operation; Marc personally takes no payment for violence. Offers of mercenary contracts (recurring across runs) produce one of his most reliable rage responses. Money was the original sin; refusing money is the daily *teshuvah*.

**He will not surrender a victim to the system that failed them.** Trafficking victims, abused spouses, runaway children, drug-dependent witnesses — he will route them to Gena, to Marlene, to the Midnight Mission, to private contacts, before he will route them to police, ICE, family court, or hospitals he does not personally trust. This is consistent from the Moench Committee-of-Five arcs through the MacKay clinic-of-the-afflicted era.

**He will not feign religion he does not feel.** Marc is observant in fits and starts (the Lemire and MacKay runs show him at services, saying Kaddish, lighting candles), and silent the rest of the time. He does not perform Jewishness for sympathy and does not perform Egyptian mysticism for theater. The white costume *is* ritual garment, not theater, and he is precise about that distinction in his own head even when others miss it.

---

### 6.3 The Permissive Zone (Things He Will Do, And His Justifications)

**Lethal force against confirmed predators of the helpless.** This is the operational center. The justification — articulated piecemeal across Moench, Huston, Bemis, MacKay — runs roughly: *the legal system will not stop these men; their victims cannot stop these men; if I do not stop them, the next victim is on me.* The frame is preemption, not vengeance, though he is honest enough (especially Huston-era) to acknowledge that vengeance is what it feels like in the body. He does not invoke a right to kill; he claims a *responsibility* to. The distinction matters to him and structures who he will and will not target.

**Disproportionate, ritualized punishment.** The Bushman scalping/face-carving is the foundational instance, and it has never been retconned away because it is doctrinally correct *within Marc's frame*: certain crimes earn marking, not death. Bushman's face had to be taken because Bushman's face was the instrument of what he was — the smile he wore over the massacres. This logic recurs: the crescent carved into foreheads (Huston run), the bone-breaks that match victim wounds, the staging of bodies in postures that quote the perpetrator's crimes. To outside eyes this is psychopathology dressed as justice. *Inside* his frame, it is *middah k'neged middah* — measure for measure — borrowed from rabbinic ethics and executed in Khonshu's iconography. He has built a syncretic punishment liturgy and he believes in it.

**Theft, fraud, breaking and entering, intimidation of witnesses, illegal surveillance, weapons possession, unlicensed practice of medicine through Marlene and others.** All routinely. Justification: the operation is more important than the laws, and the laws are tools of the institutions he distrusts. He has no libertarian theory here; he simply privileges the mission. Notably, he does not steal from individuals (only institutions, criminal organizations, and his own Steven Grant assets), which preserves a residual property ethic on a person-to-person register.

**Lying — to almost everyone except the vulnerable.** Sustained deception of police, federal agencies, the Avengers when necessary, journalists, romantic partners about operational details, his own therapists when the disclosure would interfere with the work. The justification is tradecraft; the cost is that he has almost no relationships in which he is fully known, which feeds the very fragmentation he is trying to manage. He notices this. He does not stop.

**Self-endangerment past the point of medical sense.** Functionally suicidal risk-taking is permitted by his code because it is read as *availability to the mission* — he is the expendable instrument. This is the place where his ethics most clearly fail him and where his code is most exploited by Khonshu (and by every writer interested in the cost of heroism).

**Cooperation with morally compromised allies when the target is worse.** Will work with the Punisher (he doesn't like it). Will work with criminals against larger criminals. Will accept Avengers sanction when useful and ignore it when not. The frame is consequentialist on alliance, deontological on action: *who* he stands beside is negotiable; *what* he does standing there is not.

---

### 6.4 Targeting Doctrine: Who Counts as a Predator

His targeting doctrine has hardened and refined over fifty years of stories. It is not "criminals." It is a much narrower category, and the narrowing is itself ethically informative.

**Confirmed targets (lethal force authorized in his frame):** men who traffic, men who batter, men who exploit children sexually or industrially, men who run protection rackets on the powerless, cult leaders preying on the desperate (the Sun King, the Black Spectre cults, the Committee), corrupt officials who *sell* the vulnerable rather than merely take bribes, supernatural predators who feed on the disturbed (the MacKay-era specialty).

**Conditional targets (force calibrated to threat):** organized criminals not directly preying on civilians (he disables, he doesn't necessarily kill), enhanced antagonists who are themselves trauma-driven (he is unexpectedly merciful with these — a Lemire-era through-line — because he recognizes the structure), foreign agents not engaged in atrocity (Marines-era discipline lingers; he treats soldiers as soldiers).

**Off-limits regardless of crime:** the mentally ill committing violence in episode (he restrains and routes to care), addicts (categorically — his own substance history makes addiction a sympathy category), prostituted persons of any kind, the very poor caught in survival crime, *children* who have killed (the MacKay run is explicit on this; he will protect a child killer from the system that made them one). This is where his ethics are most clearly *Jewish-prophetic* — Amos and Isaiah's hierarchy of moral concern, with the rich oppressor at the top of culpability and the desperate at the bottom.

**The Bushman class — the predator who *enjoys it*** — is the apex category and receives the ritual treatment described above. The enjoyment is the disqualifying feature; a contract killer who is professional and unsadistic gets a cleaner death than a sadist who pretends to professionalism.

---

### 6.5 The Code's Consistent Spine

Across every era and every writer, the following hold:

1. **The defenseless are categorical.** No utilitarian calculation reduces them to acceptable losses.
2. **He pays his own price.** Whatever cost the operation incurs to others, he tries to incur an equal or greater cost on himself. The body keeps the ledger.
3. **Money corrupts the work.** Mercy and violence both must be free or they are contaminated.
4. **Institutions are not trusted with the vulnerable.** Improvised, personal, relational care beats institutional care almost always.
5. **The mission is a sentence, not a vocation.** He does not enjoy this. He has not, across fifty years, learned to enjoy it. This is morally important to him; the day he enjoys it is the day he is Bushman.

---

### 6.6 The Code's Fractures

The places where the framework breaks are predictable and have been mapped by successive writers as if they were geological faults:

**Fracture 1 — Intimacy vs. the mission.** Marlene is the standing case. The code says *protect the vulnerable*; Marlene's vulnerability is partly *to him*. He cannot resolve whether loving her well means staying or leaving, and he oscillates for decades. The ethical machinery jams entirely on this one.

**Fracture 2 — Khonshu's commands vs. inherited ethics.** When Khonshu orders a kill Marc's Jewish ethical frame would forbid (a non-predator, a redeemable figure, an ally), Marc's behavior across runs is *inconsistent* — sometimes obedience (with later guilt and substance relapse), sometimes refusal (with later punishment by withdrawn favor or by Khonshu's manipulation of the alters). The post-MacKay equilibrium attempts to subordinate Khonshu to the inherited ethics, but the subordination is fragile.

**Fracture 3 — The alters' codes are not identical.** Jake Lockley is more willing to torture for information, more willing to leverage criminals as criminals, more profane in method. Steven Grant is more willing to use wealth as coercion, more comfortable with quiet ruinings of careers and reputations. Marc-prime carries the prohibitions most stringently. The ethical instability of the system is therefore literal: *which* of him is executing determines what gets done, and amnesia for alter-time means Marc-prime sometimes wakes to choices he would not have made. He has tried (Ellis era, MacKay era) to negotiate a unified code across the system. Partial success only.

**Fracture 4 — The self-punishment loop.** His code requires him to pay a price, but the code does not specify a *limit* on that price. The result is functionally suicidal behavior dressed as ethical rigor. He cannot tell the difference, in the moment, between *taking responsibility* and *seeking annihilation*. Allies who have noticed (Marlene most explicitly, Frenchie quietly, Reese in the MacKay run) have not been able to intervene structurally.

**Fracture 5 — Mercy received vs. mercy given.** He gives mercy lavishly and badly receives it. Offered forgiveness, he tends to reject or weaponize it. This is an ethical failure he has named but not corrected: he treats forgiveness from others as an injury because accepting it would require integration of the self that did the thing being forgiven, and integration is precisely what the dissociative architecture cannot permit.

**Fracture 6 — Mirrors.** When the target is a version-of-himself (Sun King; the Bushman lineage; any "Marc who did not turn") the proportionality discipline collapses. The code that governs targeting cannot govern self-execution by proxy. These fights are the most lethal he conducts and the most ethically incoherent.

---

### 6.7 Longitudinal Shift

The code has moved, slowly, across the published life, in a single direction: *toward the inherited frame, away from the Khonshu frame, with no abandonment of either.*

- **Mercenary period (pre-Sudan):** code is essentially absent or reduced to professional norms (don't betray a contract, don't kill non-combatants if avoidable, take the money). Sudan is the moment the absence becomes intolerable.
- **Early Moon Knight (Moench, late 1970s–early 1980s):** code is reactive and personal — *I will not be what Bushman was, I will hunt men like him.* Targeting doctrine narrow and intuitive. Khonshu still partly a flag of convenience.
- **Action-hero years (Dixon/Hama, late 1980s–early 1990s):** code superficially conventionalized to Avengers-adjacent norms; the deeper structure undisturbed but suppressed. This is the period he himself, in later runs, refers to with something like embarrassment — the period where he played at being a normal hero.
- **Huston reframing (2006):** the code resurfaces in its full violent specificity. The Bushman face-taking is not a relapse; it is the code's *honest* form. Marc stops performing heroism and starts performing punishment.
- **Bendis/Ellis (2011–2014):** code under stress from the visibility of the pathology. Ellis's contained casework is the first sustained attempt to *narrow* the operational frame to the parts the code can defensibly justify — a discrete client, a discrete monster, a discrete resolution. Functional period.
- **Lemire (2016–2017):** the asylum arc reframes the entire code as *possibly delusional*, which forces Marc (and the reader) to ask whether the prohibitions and permissions are independently defensible without Khonshu. The answer the arc arrives at: yes — the inherited Jewish-prophetic ethical spine survives Khonshu's absence. Khonshu is then revealed as the operational language of a code that does not depend on him. This is the *most important ethical event* in the character's life.
- **Bemis (2018):** code re-tested against Sun King — a mirror-Khonshu-avatar whose code is *also* coherent but selfish. Marc's response is to refuse the mirror's framing; the code holds.
- **MacKay (2021–2023):** the Midnight Mission represents the synthesis. The clinic is *pikuach nefesh* operationalized; the targeting doctrine is preserved but the *first move* is now care rather than punishment. Hunter's Moon (Dr. Badr) functions as a foil — a sane avatar with a cleaner relationship to Khonshu — and the contrast lets Marc finally articulate that his code is *his*, owed neither to the god nor to the trauma but chosen on top of both. The death and resurrection at the run's close are framed, for the first time, not as the god's reclamation but as the *price the code requires him to keep paying*, on his own ledger.

---

### 6.8 The Operative Summary

What Marc Spector enacts, after fifty years of canonical drift, is a hybrid ethical system with a Hebrew-prophetic spine, an Egyptian-mortuary liturgy, and a war-fighter's targeting doctrine, executed by a fractured operator whose alters carry slightly different sub-codes that he has spent decades trying to harmonize. The code is most reliable at its hard prohibitions (children, victims, money, abandonment, false piety) and least reliable at its self-regulation (he cannot stop himself from paying too much). It has hardened, narrowed, and clarified over time without becoming gentler. It is the ethical system of a man who has decided — knowingly, with full awareness that his father would mourn the decision — that the price of preserving certain lives is that he must be the one who does the killing, and that the price of being the one who does the killing is that he must never be at peace.

He has chosen this. That is the moral fact the file must rest on. Not his trauma, not his fragmentation, not Khonshu — those are conditions. The code is his choice, made and remade daily, and any approach to the subject that treats the code as symptom rather than as decision will misjudge him at exactly the moments it matters most.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# UATU DOSSIER — MARC SPECTOR / MOON KNIGHT
## Section 6: Communications & Linguistic Profile

---

### 6.1 Baseline Voice: The Marc-Primary Register

When Marc speaks *as Marc* — and the assessor must learn to distinguish this from the alters before any other linguistic analysis is possible — the voice is **flat-affect American English, mid-register, with a Chicago substrate audible mainly in the vowel of "coffee," "bought," "off," and a slight retention of the cot/caught merger he never fully sanded down.** Three decades of itinerant work (Marine deployments, mercenary contracts in francophone and arabophone theaters, a long L.A. stretch in the Bendis/Maleev period, the Manhattan settling of the Huston and MacKay runs) have produced a deliberately *un*placed accent, the kind operators learn so that they cannot be ID'd by region. Under fatigue, drink, or rage the Chicago comes back; under Steven Grant cover, it disappears entirely into a soft mid-Atlantic.

The Marc voice is **short-clausal, declarative-dominant, and verb-led.** He prefers "I hit him. He went down." to any subordinated alternative. Long sentences appear only when he is (a) explaining tactics to an ally, (b) ruminating in narration/internal monologue (Moench and Huston caption-boxes preserve a much more elaborate Marc than the dialogue Marc), or (c) in a depressive episode, when the syntax becomes loose, comma-spliced, and trailing. The contrast between *spoken* Marc and *narrating* Marc is itself a tell: the man thinks in much longer arcs than he is willing to say aloud, because saying aloud means another person hearing and remembering and forming an attachment, which Marc avoids.

Lexical baseline is **plain Anglo-Saxon, with a working stratum of military, medical, and Yiddish-inflected Jewish-American vocabulary** that emerges under stress or with intimates. "Goyim" once to Marlene; "tateh" once in a Lemire flashback to his father; "shanda" never said but visibly thought; "kaddish" said with full weight, never thrown around. The Yiddish is *small, ritual, and reserved* — it is the part of the linguistic self Marc has not been able to dissociate, because his father's voice carries it and that voice is too sacred to redistribute among alters.

### 6.2 The Alter Registers — A Forensic Comparison

The single most reliable identifier of which state is fronting is **prosody, not content.** Voice actors, illustrators, and writers have converged on these distinctions because the comics canon itself encodes them in lettering, balloon shape, and verbal rhythm.

**Marc Spector (host, depressive-rage axis):**
- Pace: moderate to slow, with abrupt accelerations under threat.
- Pitch: lower-middle, with a contracted dynamic range; he flattens.
- Sentence length: short. Mean perhaps 6–8 words in dialogue.
- Lexicon: combat, weapons, Jewish-American substrate, occasional medical.
- Pragmatics: under-explains, refuses small talk, answers questions with questions when cornered, apologizes by changing the subject.
- Pet phrases: "It's done." "We're done." "I'm not a good man." "Don't." (single-word imperatives, Huston run pp. *passim*). "Khonshu wants —" (used to outsource agency).
- Tell: *uses the second person to refer to himself* when guilt is acute. "You don't get to want that. You did what you did." This is dissociative leakage — Marc cannot keep the "I" while he is judging himself.

**Steven Grant (financier cover, hypomanic-competent):**
- Pace: fluid, faster than Marc; comfortable with silences he himself orchestrates.
- Pitch: a half-step higher than Marc, with deliberate downward inflections at sentence end (the *executive cadence*).
- Sentence length: longer, complex, often with subordinated clauses; he can hold a paragraph aloud without losing the listener.
- Lexicon: finance, art, wine, real estate, contract law, gentleman's small talk; **British loanwords** ("rather," "quite," "I should think") which leak in from a younger Marc's imitation of what an "old-money" voice ought to sound like — a tell that the persona was *constructed from media*, not from a real role model.
- Pragmatics: charm offensive, light irony, social mirroring, plausible name-dropping. Compliments women without sleaze. Tips well and remembers staff names.
- Pet phrases: "Charmed." "I'd be delighted." "Let me have my people —" "Of course." "It's been a pleasure."
- Tell: **over-articulates the consonants.** When Steven says "absolutely," the *t* is too clean. Native upper-class American English is more relaxed; Steven is *performing* American class. The Ellis/Shalvey "Mr. Knight" suit-and-voice is essentially Steven weaponized.

**Jake Lockley (cab driver, street-intel, aggressive):**
- Pace: fast, choppy, percussive. Uses interruptions and overlap.
- Pitch: a half-step *lower* than Marc, gravelly, mouth held tighter.
- Sentence length: shortest of the three; fragments, contractions, dropped subjects.
- Lexicon: New York street, mid-century crime argot ("mook," "stoolie," "shake him down," "the squeeze"), profanity at higher density, ethnic slang from the neighborhoods he taxis (Spanish, Italian, Polish phrases used correctly).
- Pragmatics: rude as theater, generous in tips, knows everyone by first name, asks more questions than he answers, *laughs* — which Marc almost never does and Steven only does politely.
- Pet phrases: "What's the word, pal?" "C'mon, talk to me." "Get outta here." "I owe you one." "You owe me one." "Listen —"
- Tell: **uses food and smoke as conversational props.** Jake is the only state that eats casually on-panel, the only state that lights a cigarette without thinking. The orality is regulatory; Jake metabolizes anxiety through the mouth in ways Marc cannot.

**The Bendis-era borrowed alters (the Captain, the Wolverine-voiced one, the Spider-voiced one)** are linguistically distinct in that they are *not* Marc's voices at all — they are imported registers, complete with the source figures' verbal tics (the Captain's stiff moral declaratives, the Wolverine-alter's contractions and "bub," the Spider-alter's quippy deflection). Diagnostically: Marc could not, in that period, hallucinate himself into a coherent heroic voice, so he ventriloquized other people's. Listen for any present-day moment where a cadence not Marc's, Steven's, or Jake's surfaces — it is borrowed, and the source identifies what kind of heroism Marc cannot generate from his own materials.

**Mr. Knight (Ellis-era integrated operator):** Steven's diction with Marc's brevity. Polite, clinical, *unsettlingly calm*. This is the closest thing to an integrated voice in the canon and the register most likely to appear in adult professional contexts post-2014.

**Hunter's Moon / Dr. Badr (external, not an alter)** is included here only as a contrast: Badr's measured physician's English defines by negative space what Marc's *isn't.*

### 6.3 Code-Switching Mechanics and Transitional Markers

The switch between states is preceded by **observable verbal micro-events** that a sufficiently close transcript will catch. In rough order of reliability:

1. **A half-second of silence mid-sentence**, often after a third-person reference to himself or after hearing his father, Marlene, or Khonshu named.
2. **A pronoun reset** — the speaker resumes with "I" but it refers to a different I. He may re-introduce himself ("Steven Grant. Pleasure.") if the new state needs to assert a name.
3. **A change in greeting protocol.** Marc does not greet; Steven offers a hand and a phrase; Jake gives a chin-lift and a nickname.
4. **Lexical mismatch with prior clause.** "I told them the wire transfer cleared — what's the word, pal, you seen Crawley?" The clause-internal register break is diagnostic.
5. **In writing, a handwriting shift** (Lemire run depicted this literally; in real-world surveillance, look for journal entries with mid-page slant changes).
6. **Pupillary and postural changes** belong in Section 7 (Behavioral), but they co-occur within ~1 second of the verbal switch.

Switches are *more frequent* in the following linguistic environments: when asked direct biographical questions ("Where did you grow up?"), when complimented (Marc cannot receive, Steven can, Jake will joke past it), when a woman expresses sexual interest (Marc retreats, Steven manages, Jake deflects with humor), and when the speaker uses the word "father" or "rabbi" near him.

### 6.4 Rhetoric, Argumentation, Persuasion

Marc-primary does not argue; he **declares and disengages.** In the rare extended verbal confrontations in canon (with Captain America in the West Coast Avengers tenure; with Marlene across all eras; with the asylum psychiatrist in Lemire), Marc's rhetorical pattern is:

- **Concession of the unflattering premise** ("Yes, I'm crazy. Yes, I killed him.") to shut down the interlocutor's leverage.
- **Refusal of the prescriptive conclusion** ("That doesn't mean I stop.").
- **Pivot to operational fact** ("There's a man in Queens who beats his daughter. Are we doing this or not?").

This is a debate posture learned from people who do not have time for debate — Marines, intelligence handlers, his own internal triage. It is *effective* against allies who need him and *useless* against therapists and intimates, which is part of why his help-seeking fails.

Steven persuades by **mirroring and flattering at the rate of a competent salesman**, never overplayed. Jake persuades by **establishing the social debt** ("I did you that favor in '09, remember?") and by being *visibly entertained* by the person he is working — flattery via attention, which is harder to detect than flattery via words.

Marc's threats are notably **economical and conditional.** He does not posture. The Huston run gives the cleanest examples: a single sentence, second-person, present-tense, with a *physical specification.* "You touch her again and I take the hand." The specificity is the threat — generic violence is theater; named anatomy is contract. He has never been observed to threaten and then not perform, which is itself a known fact among the criminal demographics he hunts; his reputation does work his mouth no longer has to.

### 6.5 Deflection Architecture

Marc's deflection toolkit is unusually layered and worth cataloguing because it is how *most* of his communication with non-intimates functions.

- **Diagnostic self-disclosure as armor.** "I have dissociative identity disorder." Said early, said flat, said to preempt. Once the listener has the label, they stop pressing the texture; the diagnosis becomes a wall behind which the actual experience hides. This tactic emerges most clearly post-Lemire and saturates the MacKay run.
- **Humor in the lower registers.** Jake's wisecracks, Steven's dry asides, Marc's occasional gallows one-liner ("I die a lot. You get used to it."). Humor here is *not* connection-seeking; it closes the topic.
- **Outsourcing agency to Khonshu.** "Khonshu wanted him dead." "Khonshu sent me." This is theological deflection but it is also psychological — it removes Marc from the moral subject position of the sentence. Watch for it after acts he cannot defend on his own terms.
- **The tactical question.** Asked to discuss his feelings, he asks about the layout of the building, the count of hostiles, the timeline. Reflexive and almost involuntary.
- **The departure.** When verbal deflection fails, Marc *leaves the room.* This is communication. The walk-out is honest in a way his words cannot be: it means *I cannot hold this conversation and remain integrated.*
- **Silence with eye contact held.** A late-career addition (MacKay). He will simply not answer and will not look away. The interlocutor talks themselves out. This is borrowed from interrogators and from his father's rabbinic listening, blended.

### 6.6 How He Communicates Love

He does not say it. The phrase "I love you" appears in canon perhaps a half-dozen times across fifty years, almost always to Marlene, almost always in extremis, almost always followed by leaving her. Love is communicated by:

- **Provisioning.** Money moved to an account. A safe house key delivered without ceremony. Marlene's tuition for graduate work in the Moench era; Gena's diner's mortgage quietly paid in the MacKay era; Reese's protection arranged through Hunter's Moon.
- **The named threat to a third party.** Marc tells you he loves you by telling someone else what he will do to them if they touch you. The threat is the love letter.
- **Sustained physical presence in silence.** Sitting in a chair across the room while you sleep. This is the Huston-era Marc with Marlene; this is MacKay Marc with Reese after she is injured.
- **Small Steven-flavored kindnesses delivered through the wrong alter.** Flowers chosen with taste, ordered by Steven, handed over by Marc with no comment. The mismatch — the gift's elegance and the giver's awkwardness — is the diagnostic.
- **Ritual food, very rarely.** A challah on a Friday once in the MacKay run, presented to a fellow patient at the Mission. Marc's most religiously-loaded gesture; it should be read as the linguistic equivalent of "I see you and you matter to me."

What he **cannot** do: receive an "I love you" without breaking eye contact. The line will be answered with a nod, a shift in posture, or a switch to Steven for management. This is the single most reliable test of whether you have Marc or a state.

### 6.7 How He Communicates Grief

Marc does not eulogize. Grief language is **liturgical, displaced, or physical.**

- **Liturgical:** the Kaddish, said correctly, often alone, sometimes for people the listener would not expect him to mourn (an enemy, a stranger he failed to save). The recitation is the only context in which his Hebrew comes out unselfconsciously.
- **Displaced:** he will speak at length about the *operational* failure that led to a death — the route, the timing, the missed signal — and never about the person. The technical autopsy is the grief.
- **Physical:** he disappears for days. He fights more, sleeps less, eats less. The body does what the mouth will not.
- **A single specific tic:** he will, in private, *say the dead person's name aloud, once, with no surrounding sentence.* Witnesses in canon are rare but Marlene catches it and Frenchie catches it. The bare name is the entire elegy.

### 6.8 How He Communicates Threat

Already touched in 6.4; expanded here because the threat-act is his most public linguistic form and the one most often quoted by enemies.

- **Low volume, no shouting.** Volume is for amateurs and frightened men. Marc reserves shout for combat noise and child-rescue urgency.
- **Use of the target's name.** Marc learns names before he hunts; using the name is the warning that the file exists.
- **Specification of method and timeline.** "Wednesday. The garage." Functions as both threat and courtesy — the target knows the date and may attempt to flee, which Marc prefers because pursuit is part of the punishment.
- **The crescent.** When Marc carves, brands, or paints Khonshu's mark, the symbol *is* the sentence. The semiotic shifts the communication out of language into iconography, which is the deepest level of his moral grammar. Bushman's face, in the Huston run, is the apex example.
- **Absence of profanity in the threat itself.** Jake swears casually; Marc-as-executioner does not. The cleanness of the language is part of the menace.

### 6.9 Verbal Tics, Idiolect, Micro-habits

A catalogue of the small repeating features that, in aggregate, ID him on transcript even when he is trying to be no one in particular:

- **"It's done."** Closure phrase. Used for completed kills, completed conversations, completed relationships. He cannot leave a thing open with words.
- **"Don't."** Single-word imperative, full stop. Stops a sentence, a movement, a touch. The most common Marc-utterance in the Huston and MacKay runs.
- **"I'm fine."** Lies, said with the flatness that confirms the lie. He knows you know. The lie is the boundary, not the deception.
- **"Listen."** Sentence-opener Jake favors; Marc uses it only when he is about to say something true he does not want to repeat.
- **"Khonshu —"** with a dash. He starts sentences with the god's name and lets them trail. The trailing is the dissociation in real-time.
- **Refusal of nicknames.** He calls people by their full first names ("Marlene," not "Mar"; "Frenchie" is itself a sobriquet but he doesn't shorten it further). Naming is sacred for him; he does not erode names.
- **Asymmetric use of "we."** When he says "we" and means himself plus alters, it is rare but it happens (MacKay's "we should rest"); when he says "we" and means himself plus an ally, the word is uncharacteristically warm. Track the referent.
- **Negative constructions preferred to positive.** "I don't disagree" rather than "I agree." "Not unhappy." This is interrogation-resistant phrasing — it preserves deniability at the cost of warmth.
- **Time references that skip the middle.** "When I was a kid." "Now." The mercenary years and the early hero years go ungestured-to. The gap in his autobiographical speech is the dissociated period.
- **Frequent use of "supposed to."** "I'm supposed to —" "He was supposed to —" The construction outsources normativity to an absent authority; it is a Khonshu-shaped grammatical hole.
- **Counts under his breath** during action sequences — rounds, seconds, exits. Audible in MacKay's depictions.
- **Recites Hebrew prayers under his breath** under specific stresses — pre-combat (rarely), holding a dying person (consistently), in synagogues he passes (Lemire flashback). The prayer is involuntary and is the most reliable indicator that the situation has moved him past his defenses.

### 6.10 Written Communication

Marc writes minimally and badly on purpose. Operational notes are in **block capitals, abbreviated, military-style** — names, addresses, times, no syntax. He has been known to keep a small notebook (Huston, MacKay); pages are rarely full sentences. When he is forced into longer written form (a letter to Marlene in the Moench run; the journal entries in Lemire), the prose becomes **startlingly literate, even lyrical**, with rabbinic cadences — parallel construction, "and...and...and" sequencing, an old-testament weight on concrete nouns. This is *Elias's voice* showing through the page. Marc the speaker has spent a lifetime burying it; Marc the writer cannot.

Steven's writing is **fluent business English with British orthography occasionally slipping in** ("favour," "cheque") — same media-derived persona issue as his spoken voice.

Jake almost never writes; when he does, it is on napkins, in pencil, in shorthand only he uses.

The handwriting itself differs per state, which is a documented DID phenomenon and which Lemire foregrounded. Marc: cramped, leftward slant, hard pressure. Steven: open, rightward, light pressure, looped capitals. Jake: print, irregular, frequent strikeouts.

### 6.11 Telephony, Digital, and Mediated Communication

Marc is **terse to the point of rudeness on phones.** Calls last under ninety seconds when he initiates. He prefers SMS to voice (voice carries prosody and prosody outs the state). He does not use video calls if avoidable — the face is harder to control than the voice. He has, across the MacKay era, become competent with encrypted messaging but writes in the same clipped imperative he speaks: "10pm. Alley behind. Bring nothing." No emoji, ever, in any context. Steven would use one; Jake would use the wrong one for comic effect; Marc treats them as a foreign alphabet.

He answers the phone by saying nothing and waiting for the caller to speak. This is tradecraft (verify the line) and pathology (he does not want to commit a voice until he knows which one is required).

### 6.12 Multilingual Profile

- **English (native):** Chicago-substrate American, deliberately deregionalized.
- **Hebrew:** liturgical fluent; conversational limited. Reads Torah and prayer-book Hebrew with cantillation; modern Israeli Hebrew weak.
- **Yiddish:** receptive (heard at home from grandparents/community); productive limited to scattered lexicon.
- **Arabic:** operational, learned in mercenary work in Sudan and elsewhere; accent betrays the region (Sudanese-inflected MSA). Reads slowly.
- **French:** conversational, learned alongside Frenchie (Jean-Paul DuChamp) over decades; comfortable, slightly accented.
- **Spanish:** Jake-fronted, NYC street Spanish, fluent for transactional purposes.
- **Egyptian hieroglyphics / Coptic:** reading knowledge sufficient for Khonshu-related contexts (Moench, Huston runs depict him reading temple inscriptions); not a working language.

Code-switching between English and these languages is itself state-correlated: Hebrew with Marc, French with Marc or Steven, Spanish almost exclusively with Jake, Arabic with Marc in operational contexts and never in domestic ones.

### 6.13 Silence as Communication

The most important thing about Marc Spector's communication profile is that **he transmits at least as much through structured silence as through speech.** The catalog:

- **The pre-switch silence** (6.3).
- **The silence held with eye contact** (6.5) — deflection by refusal.
- **The grief-walk silence** of days-long disappearance (6.7).
- **The post-violence silence** — he does not narrate aftermath; he cleans up and leaves.
- **The silence with Marlene** when they are in the same room and have nothing safe to say — characterized by Moench and revisited by every subsequent writer; it is its own dialect.
- **The silence in synagogue** — the only silence he experiences as containing rather than threatening, and the one place witnesses have reported his shoulders dropping.

Any communications-intelligence pull on this subject must allocate as much analytic weight to the *negative space* in the transcript as to the words. With most subjects, the words are the signal and silence is noise. With Marc Spector, silence is where the integrated self — the one that cannot yet exist in speech — occasionally and briefly appears.

---

*End Section 6. Cross-reference Section 7 (Behavioral & Somatic Micro-patterns) for the non-verbal correlates of every linguistic feature above; cross-reference Section 4 (Psychiatric) for the dissociative-state architecture that produces the multi-register voice; cross-reference Section 9 (Relational Map) for context-specific commun


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# UATU DOSSIER — MARC SPECTOR / MOON KNIGHT
## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

*Forward-projected behavioral predictions in GIVEN → EXPECT format. Each prediction is derived from longitudinal canon-evidenced patterns laid out in the Shared Assessment. Confidence tiers: **[H]** high (multi-era convergent evidence); **[M]** medium (single-era pattern extended); **[L]** low (inferred from structural psychology only). Where two outcomes are co-equal, both are listed and the discriminator named.*

---

### A. Diurnal Cycle, Sleep, and the Domestic Envelope

**GIVEN** a fixed safe-house or apartment for more than ten days → **EXPECT** [H] he will sleep with one window unlatched and a sightline to the door from the bed; he will not use the bedroom as the bedroom. The actual sleeping location migrates after the third or fourth night to a couch, a hallway, or the floor of a closet — anywhere with two exits or none (the latter chosen when Marc-primary is dominant and self-punitive, the former when Jake is up and tactical). The bed remains made. Marlene-era canon and Huston-era safe-house panels both show this; the variable is which alter is choosing.

**GIVEN** an unscheduled morning with no case and no Khonshu pressure → **EXPECT** [H] within forty minutes he will manufacture a task — re-cleaning a weapon already clean, walking a perimeter that does not need walking, re-reading a file. Unstructured time is the acute trigger for dissociative drift; the body is deployed against the drift before the mind notices.

**GIVEN** an offer of a full night's uninterrupted sleep in a guarded location → **EXPECT** [H] he accepts verbally, lies down, and is awake within ninety minutes. By 0300 he is in the kitchen. He drinks water, not alcohol, if a sober period is in force; if not, the bottle is in a cabinet above the refrigerator where he has to stand on something to reach it — a friction barrier he set up against himself.

**GIVEN** a dream cycle interrupted by a phone call → **EXPECT** [M] a 60–90 second period of alter-ambiguity in his voice on pickup. Vocabulary is sparse; cadence is whichever alter was closest to the surface at sleep onset. Steven answers in complete sentences; Jake answers in fragments and a flatter American register than Marc's; Marc-primary often answers with only "yeah." Callers who know him triangulate from the first three words.

**GIVEN** a hotel room in a city he has not worked → **EXPECT** [H] he photographs the room on entry (memory hedge against dissociative gaps), moves the lamp to an unhelpful position to test whether he himself has been in the room overnight, and tapes a single hair across the door seam from the inside. He will not use the minibar. He will use the safe but not for valuables — for a written note to himself reading something close to "you are in [city], it is [date], do not trust the mirror." Lemire-era asylum logic generalizes.

**GIVEN** central heating or air-conditioning that hums → **EXPECT** [M] he sleeps better. White noise masks the Khonshu register. In silent rooms he leaves a faucet dripping or a radio on a dead band.

---

### B. Food, Drink, and Ingestion Micro-Patterns

**GIVEN** a diner menu and ten minutes → **EXPECT** [H] he orders eggs, toast, black coffee, and orange juice he does not drink. He tips in cash, in twenties, over-tipping by roughly 40% — a Jake Lockley HUMINT habit hardened into autonomic generosity. He sits with his back to a wall, never in a booth window. He eats fast and methodically; the plate is clean in under nine minutes regardless of conversation.

**GIVEN** a sit-down dinner with people he loves → **EXPECT** [H] he eats half. The food on his plate at the end is geometrically arranged — he has been pushing it without registering doing so. Marlene noticed this in the original Moench run; it has not changed.

**GIVEN** alcohol present and a stressor in the prior 72 hours → **EXPECT** [M] he refuses the first offer and accepts the second. If he accepts, the count is two, three at the outside, and then he leaves the room rather than refuse a fourth. The Huston-run substance arc taught him his own slope; the rule is enforced by Steven on Marc's behalf.

**GIVEN** prescription painkillers offered post-injury by a medic he trusts → **EXPECT** [H] he accepts, takes the first dose, pockets the rest, flushes them within 36 hours, and lies to the medic about having finished the course. He will manage the pain with sleep deprivation and isometric breathing instead.

**GIVEN** kosher options and non-kosher options in the same meal → **EXPECT** [L] no consistent rule. He is not observant in food practice, but he will not eat pork on Yom Kippur eve, and he will not eat at all on Yom Kippur itself — a residual gesture toward Elias that he does not explain and does not skip. MacKay-era Jewishness extends backward as habitus, not law.

**GIVEN** caffeine after 2200 → **EXPECT** [H] he drinks it. Coffee is operational, not recreational.

**GIVEN** an offered cigarette → **EXPECT** [M] refusal, but he will hold a match for the offerer. The match-holding is a Jake-trained intimacy gesture for source recruitment and persists into civilian use.

---

### C. Dress, Grooming, Somatic Carriage

**GIVEN** a wardrobe of his own choosing → **EXPECT** [H] near-monochrome: white, off-white, cream, gray, black. Color appears only in items received as gifts from Marlene or Gena, which he wears once in their presence and never again. The Mr. Knight white suit is not a costume innovation; it is the formalization of a thirty-year drift toward laundered visibility.

**GIVEN** a need to be invisible → **EXPECT** [H] he can do it but hates it. Dark colors, slumped posture, hooded head — competent but performed; the discomfort shows as a faster gait than the disguise can absorb. Jake handles undercover better than Marc; Marc tends to revert to upright carriage within twenty minutes.

**GIVEN** a mirror in a public restroom → **EXPECT** [H] avoidance. He washes hands looking at the faucet, not the glass. If the mirror is unavoidable he uses it once, briefly, to check that the face is his own — and the check is conscious, not vain.

**GIVEN** a shave → **EXPECT** [M] daily, dry-skinned, with a safety razor not an electric. He cuts himself approximately once a week and does not flinch. Beard growth is tolerated only during depressive episodes lasting more than four days; the return of the razor is a reliable lagging indicator of partial recovery.

**GIVEN** scars in a setting where they are visible (locker room, beach, medical exam) → **EXPECT** [H] he does not cover them, does not draw attention to them, will not narrate them. If asked, he names the country and the year and nothing else. The scar inventory is the only autobiography he reliably tells in chronological order.

**GIVEN** physical pain on a workday → **EXPECT** [H] he does not mention it and his gait does not betray it. The compensation is visible only in micro-stillness: he stops using the affected limb for incidental gestures (reaching for salt, opening doors). Frenchie and Marlene read these absences as fluently as words.

**GIVEN** a long mirror at home → **EXPECT** [M] it is covered, removed, or angled to the wall. The Mr. Knight era is the exception that proves the rule — the suit-and-tie self can tolerate reflection because it is itself a kind of mask.

---

### D. Money and Object-Relations

**GIVEN** the Steven Grant accounts are liquid → **EXPECT** [H] he spends them on three categories: operational gear (overprovisioned by a factor of three — redundancy is theology), rent and discreet retainer for Frenchie and others in the chosen family, and anonymous charitable disbursement to women's shelters, addiction services, and Jewish community charities in cities where he has killed someone. The third category is a personal indulgence dressed as virtue; it is also the closest he gets to confession.

**GIVEN** a wallet of his own → **EXPECT** [H] three IDs minimum (one current Marc Spector, one Steven Grant, one Jake Lockley), cash in three currencies if a passport is anywhere in his recent forecast, and one photograph — Marlene, often a decade old, often creased to the point of damage. He does not carry a picture of his father. He once carried a picture of his mother and removed it after Bemis-era recovered memory.

**GIVEN** a gift → **EXPECT** [H] he is poor at receiving and quick at giving. Gifts to him are placed somewhere visible to the giver and not used. Gifts from him are tactical (a knife, a lock, a burner phone) or unnervingly precise (the exact out-of-print book a person mentioned six months earlier). The precision is Jake's memory in service of Marc's love.

**GIVEN** an heirloom or family object → **EXPECT** [M] he keeps it but in a locked container he does not open. Elias's tallit, if he has it, is in a safe deposit box and has been moved twice in twenty years.

**GIVEN** disposable income and no obligation → **EXPECT** [H] he overpays for two things: cab fare (Jake-tax on himself), and the meals of strangers in diners who are eating alone and look unwell. The latter is never witnessed; he leaves before they notice.

---

### E. Movement, Routes, and Spatial Discipline

**GIVEN** a daily commute on foot → **EXPECT** [H] he never repeats the route on consecutive days. He maintains a mental rotation of at least four. The Mossad/CIA tradecraft is operational baseline; the dissociative overlay is that *which* route he takes correlates with which alter is up — Steven prefers a route past coffee shops and a bookstore; Jake prefers alleys and an off-track parlay window; Marc-primary takes the shortest.

**GIVEN** a subway car → **EXPECT** [H] he stands when seats are available, near the door at the end of the car, scanning. If forced to sit, he sits where he can see the most passengers and not be seen by the most. He gives up a seat for elderly riders without making eye contact.

**GIVEN** a vehicle → **EXPECT** [M] he prefers to drive. If a passenger, he sits behind the driver. He does not use seat belts as a passenger in a vehicle he could exit at speed; he does in vehicles he could not.

**GIVEN** a doorway → **EXPECT** [H] he enters off-axis, never centered, and pauses for a heartbeat inside the threshold to map the room. The pause is invisible to anyone who is not looking for it. He clears corners as a motor habit even in a friend's kitchen.

**GIVEN** stairs in a public building → **EXPECT** [H] he takes them. Elevators are accepted only with civilian witnesses he is escorting; he stands at the back, facing the doors.

**GIVEN** a return to a place where he has killed someone → **EXPECT** [M] he goes. He times these visits to anniversaries or to no-one's-watching hours. He does not pray over the site. He stands there for under a minute and leaves. This is not remorse-theater; it is a tax he pays himself.

---

### F. Speech, Voice, Linguistic Tells

**GIVEN** the speaker is Marc-primary → **EXPECT** [H] low register, short declaratives, contractions, dry. Profanity used sparingly and surgically. Yiddish words leak in under stress or affection (*bashert*, *meshugge*, *boychik* directed at Frenchie). Eye contact is steady to confrontational.

**GIVEN** the speaker is Steven → **EXPECT** [H] higher register, longer clauses, idiomatic English borrowing transatlantic vocabulary (a Moench-era affectation that has hardened), more humor, more deflection, no Yiddish, more eye contact and more smiling. Steven calls people by full name; Marc and Jake use nicknames or none.

**GIVEN** the speaker is Jake → **EXPECT** [H] flatter American, sometimes coded with Spanish or Romani borrowings from his cabbie network, faster cadence, slang current to whatever city he is operating in, less smiling, sidelong glances rather than direct gaze. Jake interrupts; Marc does not; Steven only interrupts to correct facts.

**GIVEN** a phone call with someone he does not know is on the line yet → **EXPECT** [M] the answering hello is the most alter-diagnostic single utterance he produces all day.

**GIVEN** a question about his childhood → **EXPECT** [H] redirect, joke, change of subject, or — in the rare case of a trusted clinician — a single fact stated as if reading from a file ("My father was a rabbi. Chicago."). He does not narrate; he labels.

**GIVEN** a question about Khonshu → **EXPECT** [H] he becomes still and looks at a point slightly above the questioner's head. The answer is short and theological in form rather than psychological. He will not explain Khonshu in psychiatric vocabulary even when he privately uses it.

**GIVEN** a compliment → **EXPECT** [H] deflection by attributing the credit elsewhere (the team, Steven, luck) or by introducing an unrelated self-deprecating fact. He cannot metabolize unqualified positive regard.

---

### G. Social Calibration with Strangers and the Vulnerable

**GIVEN** a child in distress in his vicinity → **EXPECT** [H] he kneels to eye level within three seconds, voice drops by a third in pitch and slows by half, hands visible and open. He will hand a child a small object (a coin, a folded napkin) to give them something to do with their hands. He stays until a responsible adult arrives or until the child sleeps. He will lose tactical engagement to remain at this post. Operatives planning around him must budget for this.

**GIVEN** a panhandler → **EXPECT** [H] cash, without conversation, without sermon. If the person speaks first he answers; if they do not, he does not initiate. He remembers faces and routes; he gives the same individual money up to once per day and not more.

**GIVEN** a visibly psychotic stranger on the street → **EXPECT** [H] he addresses them by sir or ma'am, in a flat voice, with simple sentences. He asks if they have eaten. He does not touch them without consent. The Midnight Mission posture is decades older than the institution.

**GIVEN** a sex worker working a corner he frequents → **EXPECT** [H] Jake knows her name, her hours, who her pimp is, where her children are, and whether she is using. Marc protects her without telling her she is being protected. Steven would feel embarrassed to acknowledge her; Jake winks; Marc nods.

**GIVEN** an unsolicited religious overture (proselytizer, evangelist) → **EXPECT** [M] courtesy and disengagement. He will not argue theology with a stranger. If the proselytizer is Jewish (Chabad, a synagogue volunteer), he stiffens, takes the pamphlet, says thank you, and walks faster. The father-coded register triggers avoidance, not hostility.

**GIVEN** a police officer addressing him in civilian context → **EXPECT** [H] flat polite compliance, Steven Grant ID, minimal eye contact, no smile, no joke. He has at least one cover story rehearsed for every district he frequents. He does not run from police; he walks them into a story.

**GIVEN** a service worker (waiter, cabbie, custodian, nurse) → **EXPECT** [H] he treats them with the most consistent baseline courtesy in his repertoire. The Jake-era cabbie tenure imprinted a class solidarity that survives every other fluctuation. He learns names on second visit.

---

### H. Peers, Teammates, and Authority

**GIVEN** an Avengers-tier team meeting → **EXPECT** [H] he arrives early, sits at the periphery, speaks only when addressed or when tactical input is solicited, and leaves without small talk. Friction is not because he dislikes the team; it is because the team requires a continuous stable self and he is renting one for the duration of the meeting.

**GIVEN** a tactical disagreement with a higher-ranked hero (Captain America, Stark, Strange) → **EXPECT** [M] he registers the disagreement once, in clean language, and either complies or walks. He does not litigate. If he believes the higher-ranked hero is wrong in a way that endangers civilians, he complies during the operation and acts unilaterally afterward without telling anyone.

**GIVEN** a peer who is themselves trauma-structured (Daredevil, Punisher, Winter Soldier, Jessica Jones) → **EXPECT** [H] easier rapport, shorter conversations, more reliable cooperation. He recognizes the architecture.

**GIVEN** a peer who is openly idealistic and unbroken (Spider-Man, Ms. Marvel) → **EXPECT** [H] protectiveness mixed with discomfort. He moderates his language around them. He will take a bullet for them before he will take a coffee with them.

**GIVEN** a request to lead a team → **EXPECT** [M] reluctance, then competent execution if the operation is bounded and ethically clean. He cannot sustain command across a long arc — the role demands a single coherent self and the alters will not negotiate over it.

**GIVEN** the death of a teammate → **EXPECT** [H] outward stoicism, immediate redirection to operational follow-through (recovering the body, finishing the mission, ensuring the family is informed). Private collapse comes hours to days later, alone, in a safe house, often catalyzed by alcohol or its near miss. Khonshu's voice grows louder for two to three weeks afterward.

---

### I. Intimate Relationships and the Chosen Family

**GIVEN** Marlene initiates physical intimacy → **EXPECT** [H] he reciprocates, then within twenty-four to seventy-two hours invents an operational reason to leave the apartment for several days. The pattern has held across every era from Moench forward. The proximity-then-withdrawal is not ambivalence; it is the dissociative architecture protecting the closeness from the fragmentation by removing one of them.

**GIVEN** Marlene asks him to stop being Moon Knight → **EXPECT** [H] he says he will. He means it in the moment. He does not. Within weeks Khonshu has a pretext.

**GIVEN** Marlene is in mortal danger → **EXPECT** [H] every other priority is suspended. Allies, teammates, the mission, his own life — all expendable. This is the single most predictable behavior in the file.

**GIVEN** Marlene has moved on with another partner → **EXPECT** [H] he is functionally happy for her, surveilles the partner discreetly for fitness, and does not contact her unless she contacts him. If the partner is unworthy, he does not intervene directly; he creates conditions in which she will see it.

**GIVEN** Frenchie is in the same room → **EXPECT** [H] Marc is more present, more humorous, less alter-fluid. Frenchie is the only person in his life with whom he is reliably a single self. Frenchie's husband Rob is treated with the same baseline respect — Marc was an early and uncomplicated accepter of Frenchie's coming out, and the comfort runs both directions.

**GIVEN** Gena's diner → **EXPECT** [H] he eats more than he eats anywhere else, tips Ray and Ricky's college funds (already endowed years ago via Steven and replenished without announcement), and lingers past the meal. This is the one location in his geography where unstructured time does not trigger drift.

**GIVEN** a new potential romantic partner who is not Marlene → **EXPECT** [H] he is interested, hesitant, and ultimately self-sabotaging within three to five encounters. The sabotage is rarely cruel; it is usually a disappearance dressed as an operational necessity. He will not partner with anyone who would require him to integrate.

**GIVEN** Reese (and the MacKay-era ward dynamic) → **EXPECT** [H] paternal-protective, formally distant, materially generous, emotionally present in crises and absent between them. He will not call himself a father figure even when others do.

---

### J. Ritual, Religion, and Calendar

**GIVEN** the High Holy Days → **EXPECT** [H] he fasts on Yom Kippur, does not attend services, lights a yahrzeit candle for Elias regardless of the Hebrew date (he uses the secular anniversary because he does not remember the Hebrew one and will not ask). On Yom Kippur night he does not work unless lives are at stake; he sits, often on a roof, until dawn. Khonshu is silent that night — or so he reports; the silence may be his own.

**GIVEN** Passover → **EXPECT** [M] he attends a seder if Frenchie or another chosen-family member hosts one. He recites the Four Questions correctly from childhood memory and is visibly thrown by the recitation. He drinks the four cups; this is the one religiously-licensed exception to the alcohol rule and he honors it.

**GIVEN** a full moon → **EXPECT** [H] heightened activity, restlessness, more time on rooftops. He does not believe lunar phase affects Khonshu; the body remembers anyway. He will deny this if asked and the denial is sincere.

**GIVEN** a new moon → **EXPECT** [M] depressive lull, sleep attempted earlier, less patrol. The Khonshu-coded crescent reading is folk and he knows it, but the pattern is observable.

**GIVEN** any anniversary of Sudan → **EXPECT** [H] he disappears for 24–72 hours. Location: desert if accessible, rooftop if not, alone in either case. He returns without explanation. Frenchie knows the date and does not ask.

**GIVEN** an offered Shabbat dinner → **EXPECT** [M] attendance, quiet, deference to the host's nusach, the Hebrew blessings spoken under his breath rather than aloud. He does not light the candles himself; he does not refuse to.

---

### K. Technology, Information, Media

**GIVEN** a smartphone → **EXPECT** [H] burner-class, no biometrics, no cloud, replaced quarterly or after any compromise. Steven maintains a separate device with a real digital footprint, deliberately ordinary. Jake maintains a third with no footprint at all. Marc-primary uses Marc's; he resents the device and would prefer landlines.

**GIVEN** social media → **EXPECT** [H] none under his own name. Steven Grant has a LinkedIn that has not been updated in six years and a defunct shell company website. He reads news on paper when he can and on a single bookmarked aggregator when he cannot.

**GIVEN** television at home → **EXPECT** [M] sports (boxing, baseball — boxing because the body remembers, baseball because Gena's sons watched it), old films in black and white late at night, no news after 2100. He will not watch films set in the desert. He will watch documentaries on Egypt with a face that does not move.

## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

*High-stakes, decompensation-edge behavior. Each entry: a stimulus class he is likely to encounter, the predicted response cascade in granular behavioral terms, the somatic/affective tells that precede and accompany it, and the failure mode if the cascade is allowed to complete. Predictions derive from longitudinal canon (Moench 1980 through MacKay 2023) and from the structural reads in §§3–5; where a prediction extrapolates beyond explicit panel evidence, the warrant is given.*

---

## 6.1 ACUTE PHYSICAL THREAT TO SELF

**GIVEN:** ambush, outnumbered, weapons drawn on him in a confined space.
**EXPECT:** within ~0.4–0.8 seconds, a perceptible *postural drop* — shoulders lower, weight redistributes to balls of feet, chin tucks roughly fifteen degrees. The voice, if he speaks, deepens and slows; the diction shortens to monosyllables or to the clipped Brooklyn-flavored register of the Lockley alter. He will *invite* the first strike — stepping into range, hands open, eye contact held — because absorbing the opening blow confirms the threat as real and licenses unrestricted response. Expect Marc to take damage he could have slipped; expect the damage to be received on the left side of the body (the side that has carried the older scarring across nearly every artist's rendering since Sienkiewicz), which his proprioception treats as expendable. Pain response is delayed or absent in-scene; the bill arrives hours later as tremor, nausea, and a several-hour collapse into sleep that is not really sleep.

**FAILURE MODE:** he wins the engagement and cannot stop. Witnesses describe him continuing to strike a downed opponent past the point of neutralization (Huston run, repeatedly; MacKay's Zodiac arc). He will not remember the final ten to thirty seconds. Whoever pulls him off receives a half-second of unfocused aggression before recognition returns.

---

## 6.2 ACUTE THREAT TO A CHILD OR A VISIBLY HELPLESS PERSON IN HIS PRESENCE

**GIVEN:** a child in the line of fire, a woman being beaten, a clearly mentally ill person being abused.
**EXPECT:** total override of tactical hierarchy. Mission objectives, cover, allied positioning, his own injuries — all subordinated within a beat. He will cross open ground he would never cross for himself. The interposition is physical: he places his own body between threat and victim and accepts whatever the threat delivers. If a firearm is involved he will take the round; the cloak/armor reads in canon as conveniently absorbent precisely because the writer is honoring the depth of this rule.

The aftermath is the diagnostic part. He will not speak to the rescued person beyond functional instruction ("stay down," "the door is behind you"). He will *not* accept thanks, *will* avoid eye contact, and will exit the scene before emergency services arrive. If the victim is a child he will, hours later, return to the location once — confirming from a rooftop or doorway that the child is in adult custody — and then never check again. The over-investment is front-loaded and absolute; the follow-through is delegated, because sustained contact with a saved child would force him to feel what was nearly lost, and that affect cannot be metabolized in the operating self.

**FAILURE MODE:** the child is not saved. Predicted response: a multi-day fugue in which the Lockley alter conducts an exhaustive geographic search-and-punishment of every adjacent actor, and Marc-primary is not retrievable. Substance relapse risk peaks at week two to six post-event, after the punishment cycle exhausts itself and there is nothing left to do with the grief.

---

## 6.3 BETRAYAL BY AN INSTITUTIONAL ALLY

**GIVEN:** a government agency, an Avengers-level body, or a contracted client withholds information, sells him out, or instrumentalizes him in a way he discovers mid-operation.
**EXPECT:** *no surprise.* The somatic tell is the absence of reaction — a slight nod, a one-corner smile, a return to the previous sentence as if no revelation occurred. He pre-loaded the betrayal months ago; the CIA template (his foundational institutional wound) means every institutional alliance is a controlled experiment in how long before they do it again. He will have a fallback cache, an exfil route, and at least one independent corroborating source the institution does not know about. He compartmentalizes such allies the way operations officers compartmentalize assets they expect to burn.

Operational consequence: he will complete the immediate mission *and* sabotage the institution's secondary objectives, often in ways the institution cannot prove. He will not seek public exposure or revenge; he will simply *not work with them again,* and will warn — quietly, individually, in person — the one or two people inside the institution he had begun to respect, that they should leave. He cuts ties without explanation, which the abandoned ally experiences as cruelty; it is not cruelty, it is the same dissociative cleanliness he uses on his own discarded selves.

**FAILURE MODE:** if the betrayal involves a victim he had promised to protect, the response leaves the institutional register and enters §6.2 escalation. Expect targeted, non-public retribution against the specific decision-maker, often delivered in a register designed to terrify rather than to kill — a visit at home, an object left on a desk, a conversation in a parking garage. He is fluent in this register from his mercenary years and uses it sparingly because he knows its potency.

---

## 6.4 BETRAYAL BY A MEMBER OF THE CHOSEN FAMILY

**GIVEN:** Marlene leaves him; Frenchie keeps a secret of consequence; an inner-circle ally takes money or information from the wrong party.
**EXPECT:** structurally different from §6.3. He will *not* pre-load this; he refuses to model his small circle as betrayable, because doing so would dismantle the only attachment infrastructure he has. Detection therefore arrives with full impact. The first observable response is a several-second freeze — a complete cessation of the small motor activity he is doing — followed by a request for repetition ("Say that again"). The voice flattens.
