Granularly, this baseline produces:

- **Continued operation of a Midnight Mission–style node** (the specific real estate may change after the close of the MacKay arc, but the *function* — a public-facing intake point for those who cannot go to hospitals, police, or the Avengers — will reconstitute somewhere, because the function is now load-bearing for his psyche). Expect a second clinic, a satellite, or a successor frame within 18–36 months of any forced closure.
- **Stable working alliances** with Hunter's Moon / Dr. Badr (the sane counter-avatar functions as Marc's reality-testing partner; he will keep this man close, even as he resents the implicit comparison), Reese (street-recruited surrogate-daughter dynamic; the protective drive is fully engaged), and Soldier (the dog — non-trivial; a non-verbal attachment object that bypasses every relational defense he has, and which any forward planner should treat as a genuine therapeutic asset).
- **Marlene held at a fixed distance** — close enough to be reached, far enough to be unintegrated. The probability of full reconciliation is low; the probability of intermittent reunion under crisis is high. Expect periodic returns, each shorter than the last, each ending without bitterness — the relationship has settled into a register that costs neither of them what it used to.
- **Steven Grant alter** continues as financial and social interface; expect him to expand, not contract, as the operation institutionalizes. Funds need managing; charters need signing; respectable rooms need entering. Steven thrives on this and his airtime will grow.
- **Jake Lockley alter** remains the wet-work and HUMINT specialist, but his autonomy is the *single most volatile variable* in the system (see 6.3). Baseline assumes Jake stays contained within the team frame. He has, demonstrably, other plans.
- **A continued slow rise in self-deprecating humor and a slow decline in performative self-loathing.** The Ellis/MacKay-era Marc has learned that calling himself crazy out loud no longer functions defensively the way it did in the Huston era; the audience has caught up. He will, by necessity, find subtler tells.
- **Annual or biennial near-death event**, presented as Khonshu-mediated, recoverable. The body's capacity to absorb these is finite and decreasing (see 6.2).

This is not a happy forecast. It is a *sustainable* one — which, for this subject, is the better part of victory.

---

### 6.2 The Somatic Clock

The single most underweighted variable in long-horizon assessment is the **body**. Khonshu's resurrections are not regenerative in the Wolverine sense; they restore *function* but do not reverse *accumulation*. The cumulative load (Section 2) is now approaching the regime in which professional fighters retire, neurologically, whether they want to or not.

Expected somatic developments, 5–15 year window:

- **Progressive emotional dyscontrol** consistent with CTE-spectrum change: shortened fuse, increased paranoid ideation around perceived betrayal, episodic depressive deepening unresponsive to his usual coping (i.e., the work no longer fixes it the way it used to). This will be experienced *by him* as Khonshu growing louder or more capricious, because his interpretive frame routes all internal dysregulation through the god-channel.
- **Sleep architecture collapse.** Already poor. Worsening sleep will potentiate both dissociative switching and Khonshu-salience. The single highest-leverage non-psychiatric intervention available to anyone trying to help him is *sleep* — and he will refuse it, because unconsciousness is when the alters reshuffle without his oversight.
- **Chronic pain returning to Huston-era levels** within a decade, probability high. Prior opioid history makes relapse the central risk. Expect him to seek physical therapies, ascetic disciplines, or supernatural pain management before he accepts pharmacology — pride and history both fight the prescription pad.
- **A genuine cardiac or neurological event** that *cannot* be cleanly narrativized as Khonshu's doing. This will be the most clarifying medical event of his late life; it will force a confrontation with mortality on terms the theology cannot fully metabolize.
- **A point — call it the somatic terminus** — at which the operator can no longer be the body in the field. He has roughly a decade before this becomes acute. The question of succession (6.6) becomes existential at that point.

---

### 6.3 The Jake Lockley Problem

Across multiple runs, but especially foregrounded in the MacKay material, Jake has been observed **operating without Marc's knowledge** — maintaining safe houses, vehicles, contacts, and *kill lists* that Marc-self is not party to. This is the single most destabilizing element in the system and the most likely vector for catastrophe.

Three trajectories for Jake, in descending order of probability:

1. **Continued covert autonomy with deniable overlap.** Jake does the things Marc cannot consciously authorize, Marc benefits from the results without owning them, the system maintains plausible internal deniability. This is the *current* configuration. It is unstable but functional. Expect periodic ruptures when Jake's actions create consequences Marc-front must answer for.
2. **Jake becomes the dominant alter for an extended period.** Triggered by a sufficient injury to Marc-front (a death of a protected figure, a major betrayal, a Marlene-loss). This produces a 3–18 month window in which the operator is materially more lethal, less discriminating, and harder for allies to reach. Hunter's Moon and Reese are the only individuals positioned to recognize the switch quickly and respond without escalating it.
3. **Jake "secedes."** The dissociative-disorder literature recognizes alters that effectively split off and pursue independent goals against the host's wishes. The MacKay run has flirted with this. If it occurs at scale, it is functionally a **villain origin from inside the subject's own skull** — and the resulting figure would have all of Marc's training, none of his restraint, and total knowledge of his weaknesses. This is the single worst-case psychiatric scenario in the file.

The forward-planning implication: any therapeutic frame that attempts to *eliminate* Jake will accelerate scenario 3. Any frame that *negotiates with* Jake — gives him stated work, channeled outlets, acknowledged status within the team — reduces it. This is counterintuitive to standard integration models and is the area where conventional psychiatry would do the most harm.

---

### 6.4 The Khonshu Variable

The forward course of the relationship with Khonshu admits four broad outcomes; the subject has, at different points, hovered near each.

- **Continued ambivalent service** (baseline). Marc as avatar, negotiating, occasionally defying, mostly complying. The role he has held longest and is best at. Highest stability, moderate moral cost.
- **Full rupture.** Marc renounces, Khonshu retaliates by withdrawal of favor or active opposition. Historically these episodes have been short and ended in reconciliation, but a *durable* rupture is increasingly possible as Marc's self-concept becomes less dependent on Khonshu's validation. Risks: loss of the externalized regulator that the alters need (Khonshu functions, however abusively, as the system's organizing principle); replacement by a *worse* organizing principle (a different god, a different obsession, a different abusive structure — the slot will not stay empty).
- **Transformation of the relationship.** The MacKay run has begun rehearsing this: Marc as Khonshu's avatar but *on terms set by Marc*, with the Midnight Mission as a counter-proposal to pure vengeance. This is the *growth* trajectory and the one most worth supporting. It does not require Khonshu to be real or unreal; it requires Marc to occupy the priest-role rather than the weapon-role within the same theology.
- **Replacement of Marc as avatar.** Khonshu has, canonically, sought other avatars (Hunter's Moon is one such; Marc himself was a replacement). The deepest abandonment wound Marc carries is paternal; being *replaced* by Khonshu would activate that wound directly and is one of two events (the other being Marlene's death) that could trigger psychotic-grade decompensation.

The single highest-leverage cognitive move available to Marc — and the one his late-period writing keeps reaching toward — is the recognition that **the god is real or not real is the wrong question**, and that the operative question is **what kind of priest he wants to be.** Once that reframe is stable, the relationship becomes negotiable for the first time in his life.

---

### 6.5 Relational Fork Points

- **Marlene.** Two paths. (a) She remains a fixed, intermittent presence — the baseline — and dies eventually of ordinary causes or violence-adjacent ones. Her death is one of the two **decompensation-grade events** in his future. (b) A late reconciliation, probably initiated by her, in a register neither of them previously accepted: not partnership, not romance, but witness. The probability of (b) rises sharply if Marc successfully consolidates the priest-role frame in 6.4.
- **Frenchie.** Stable. He has weathered every prior crisis and will weather the rest. His own mortality is the relevant variable; losing Frenchie removes the only person who knew Marc *before* Khonshu.
- **Reese / surrogate-daughter figures.** This is the **growth vector most likely to actually move him**. He has shown, across forty years, a capacity for protective tenderness toward young people that does not depend on integration of his own selves. A successor / ward / inheritor relationship — whether Reese specifically or someone in her structural position — is the single relational frame in which he can practice being whole without having to *be* whole, because the relationship is hierarchical and protective rather than peer and intimate.
- **Hunter's Moon.** Mirror and brake. The presence of a *sane* avatar of the same god is a perpetual implicit reproach and also a perpetual implicit permission ("you do not have to carry this alone, and you do not have to carry it well"). Marc will alternate between resenting and relying on him. The relationship is one of the rare ones where Marc is not the most damaged person in the room he agrees to share, and that fact alone is therapeutic.
- **The Avengers and capes-adjacent peer group.** Will remain low-affinity, transactional. Do not expect meaningful peer integration; expect occasional ad-hoc coalition. The Bendis-era hallucination of Captain America, Wolverine, and Spider-Man as alters indicates how unbridgeable the gap reads to him from the inside — he can only access that peer authority by *becoming* it psychotically. He has, since, made peace with not having it.
- **The patient population of the Mission.** Increasingly load-bearing. He is becoming the man the broken come to, which structurally requires him to remain broken-but-competent. This is sustainable. It is also a trap, in that it gives him a *role-based reason not to heal further* than he already has.

---

### 6.6 Succession

Within ten to fifteen years, succession ceases to be optional. The frames available:

- **Hunter's Moon as operational successor.** Already in position; would require Khonshu's assent, which is uncertain.
- **Reese or a similar protégé as inheritor of the mantle in a renovated form.** Most psychologically meaningful to Marc — he would be giving the symbol to someone he raised into it.
- **Dispersal of the function** — the Mission outlives the man, the cape goes into a drawer, the patients are referred. Most adaptive; least likely, because Marc will resist anything that suggests the work can continue without a *body in the suit.*
- **A formal handoff via near-death (controlled).** The most likely actual mechanism: a final mission, survived by intent, after which he transitions to the *teacher* role full-time. This is the trajectory the late period of MacKay is rehearsing.

The dossier-level recommendation: **succession planning should begin now**, not at the somatic terminus, and should be framed to him as *training* rather than *replacement*. Framed as replacement, it activates the abandonment substrate and he will sabotage it.

---

### 6.7 The Two Catastrophes

Two events would, with high probability, produce irreversible decompensation:

1. **Death of a child in his direct care.** A Mission patient, Reese, a protected witness — anyone whose survival he has personally guaranteed. This crosses the only moral axiom he reliably enforces (Section 5) and routes the failure inward as confirmation of his foundational self-judgment. Expected response: Jake-dominant for an extended period, suicide-by-mission attempts, total rupture with Khonshu blamed for the failure, full substance relapse. Recovery possible but would require 2–5 years and the active intervention of every remaining attachment figure.
2. **Conclusive, undeniable demonstration that Khonshu is not real** — not Lemire's deliberately ambiguous asylum frame, but an unambiguous proof. This sounds liberatory and is not. It removes the organizing principle of the dissociative system without supplying a replacement. Expected response: catatonic collapse, then either (a) reconstruction around a new external authority (worst case: a hostile one moves into the vacated slot) or (b) — and this is the narrow growth path — slow rebuilding around the *function* Khonshu served, now consciously owned. The asymmetry is severe: the bad outcome is more probable than the good one, by roughly 3:1 on the evidence.

A third, lower-probability catastrophe: **Jake's secession** (6.3, scenario 3). Lower base rate, higher ceiling damage.

---

### 6.8 The Growth Path, Specified

What would actually move him forward — granularly, not aspirationally:

- **Continued ministry work.** The Mission frame is doing more therapeutic work than any clinician has managed in fifty years of canonical attempts. Sustain it.
- **Formal acknowledgment of the alters as a team rather than a secret.** The MacKay run has begun this; pushing it further — Steven and Jake recognized by name by his allies, given operational roles, addressed directly — reduces the dissociative *shame* that has fueled half the decompensations on record.
- **A non-violent regular practice.** He has never had one. Returning to *some* form of his father's Judaism — not as belief but as *practice*, the way recovering people use AA meetings — is the single intervention most likely to integrate the foundational fracture. The MacKay/Lemire reintroduction of his Jewish identity is the seed; it needs water. A weekly observance, a *kaddish* for his father he has avoided saying for decades, a return to a shul as a congregant rather than an avenger — any of these would do disproportionate work.
- **A real therapist, accepted as such.** He has had several, mostly antagonists or doubters. A clinician who *believes the alters and works with them* — the contemporary DID standard of care — has never been offered to him for long. Were one to be installed (Hunter's Moon could function in this role informally), the system has slack to use it.
- **A succession plan written down, in Steven's handwriting, signed.** Concrete, legal, irrevocable. This is the act that converts the role from identity to office, and converts his life from a sentence to a vocation.
- **A dog he is allowed to grow old with.** Not flippant. Soldier or a successor — a non-verbal attachment that does not require him to be coherent — is in the long run as protective of his sanity as any human in the file.

---

### 6.9 Open Questions the File Cannot Yet Close

- Whether Khonshu is, in any sense the file can verify, *real*. The dossier proceeds without resolving this, but the answer would reorganize every other forecast.
- Whether the alters predate the Sudan event by years (Lemire) or decades (Bemis flashbacks) or are present from earliest childhood (implied, never confirmed). The earlier the origin, the lower the ceiling for integration, the higher the floor for functional accommodation.
- Whether Marc has biological children he does not know about. Mercenary years; multiple identities; the question is not idle. Should one surface, it would constitute a third potential catastrophe *or* a third potential growth vector, depending entirely on the circumstances of contact.
- Whether the maternal-abuse retcon is stable canon or will be re-revised. The diagnostic picture is robust either way, but the *intervention strategy* shifts.
- Whether Randall — brother, delusion, alter, or some compound of the three — is fully accounted for in the current system roster, or remains a latent figure that could surface under stress.

---

### 6.10 Bottom Line

The subject is, against every reasonable prior, **trending toward a livable late life.** Not a healed one. Not an integrated one. A *livable* one, in which the fragmentation does work that matters, the god is held at a workable distance, the body is spent at a sustainable rate, and the people he loves are loved at a distance they can survive. The growth path is narrow but real, and it runs through ministry, succession, practice, and a small number of attachments he has already chosen well.

The catastrophe paths are also real, and the file should be re-reviewed within ninety days of any of the following triggers: a confirmed death within the Mission patient population; any Marlene health event; any indication that Jake has acted without Marc's knowledge at scale; any environmental change that disrupts sleep architecture for more than three weeks; any direct theological challenge to Khonshu's reality from a source he cannot dismiss; any approach to him by a previously-unknown blood relation.

He has spent fifty years building a structure that lets a broken man do useful work. The forward task — his, and ours in watching him — is to keep that structure standing long enough for him to teach someone else how it was built.
